8 min
The Hadith of Lifting the Pen: Proof for Legal Incapacity
Citing and authenticating the hadith of pen-lifting from three persons.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadith of lifting the pen, identify its narrators and authentication, and explain its application to the three categories, including the distinction between religious accountability and civil liability.

Core Idea
The pen of accountability is lifted from three: the sleeper, the insane, and the child — all schools agree, but civil liability remains.

This lesson examines the foundational hadith 'رفع القلم عن ثلاث' (the pen is lifted from three), which is the key proof for the legal incapacity of the sleeper, the insane, and the child. We will trace its narrations, verify its authenticity, and understand its legal implications in Hanafi fiqh. The source passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah provides both the hadith text and a practical example from the time of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the hadith wording
Learn the Arabic text of the hadith as narrated by Aisha: 'رفع القلم عن ثلاث: عن النائم حتى يستيقظ، وعن المبتلى حتى يبرأ، وعن الصبي حتى يكبر'. Note the terms: النائم (sleeper), المبتلى (the afflicted/insane), الصبي (child).
The same meaning appears in other narrations with slight wording variations.
2
Examine the chain authenticity
Review the narrators mentioned: Aisha, Ali, Abu Qatada, etc. Note that the chain includes Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman, teacher of Abu Hanifa, whom some criticized but others declared trustworthy. Understand that despite discussion, the hadith is considered sound (sahih) by many scholars.
The best chain is via Ali as recorded by Abu Dawood.
3
Understand the legal implication (raf' al-qalam)
The phrase 'رفع القلم' means the pen of recording deeds is lifted: no sin is recorded and no religious obligation is imposed. However, note that this does not automatically remove civil liability for damages.
This is a key distinction: religious accountability vs. worldly liability.
4
Apply the hadith to the story of Ali and Umar
Read the incident: Ali stopped Umar from stoning an insane woman who committed adultery, reminding him of this hadith. Umar accepted and she was released. This shows the hadith's application in criminal law: the insane are not liable for hudud punishments.
The hadith is used as a textual proof (dalil) to prevent punishment.
5
Distinguish the scope: religious vs. civil
Recognize that the hadith lifts religious accountability but does not necessarily lift civil liability. For example, if a sleeping person causes damage, he may still be required to pay compensation. This nuance will be explored in later lessons.
The Hanafi school maintains this distinction, in contrast to some other views.

Source Text

كتاب الحجر
القلم عن ثلاث اہ سے ہے جو حضرت عائشہ علی، ابوقتادہ ، ثوبان اور حضرت شداد بن اوس چھ صحابہ کرام سے بطریق صحاح و حسان
مروی ہے۔
حدیث عائشہ کی تخریج ابو داؤد، نسائی ، ابن ماجہ اور حاکم نے کی ہے:
ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: رفع القلم عن ثلاث، عن النائم حتى يستيقظ و عن المبتلى حتى يبر أو عن
الصبي حتى يكبر
آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا کہ تین شخصوں سے قلم اٹھا لیا گیا۔ ایک سوتے ہوئے سے یہاں تک بیدار ہو اور مبتلائے جنون سے یہاں تک اچھا ہو اور طفل سے یہاں تک کہ بالغ ہو۔
اس کی اسناد میں حماد بن ابی سلیمان استاد امام ابوحنیفہ ہیں جن کے محافظہ میں ابن سعد و اعمش نے کلام کیا ہے۔ لیکن امام نسائی و جلی اور یحیی بن معین وغیرہ نے ثقہ کہا ہے۔ حدیث علی بطرق متعددہ مروی ہے اور سب سے بہتر طریق امام ابو داؤد کا ہے۔
جندب
ابن وهب عن جرير بن حازم عن سليمان بن مهران (الاعمش عن ابي ظبيان عن حصين بن جندر عن ابن عباس قال: مر على بن ابى طالب بمجنونة بنى فلان و قد زنت فامر عمر بن الخطاب برجمها فردها على وقال لعمر يا امير المؤمنين اترجم هذه؟ قال: نعم، قال اوما تذكر ان رسول الله قال: رفع القلم عن ثلاث عن المجنون المغلوب على عقله و عن النائم حتى يستيقظ و عن الصبى حتى يحتلم ، قال : صدقت، فخلى سبيلها. حضرت ابن عباس فرماتے ہیں کہ حضرت علی کا گذر ایک قبیلہ کی دیوانی عورت پر ہوا جس نے زنا کیا تھا ، حضرت عمر نے اس کے رجم کا حکم دیا تو حضرت علی نے اس کی تردید کی اور کہا امیر المومنین کیا آپ اس کو سنگسار کریں گے؟ فرمایا: ہاں ، حضرت علی نے کہا۔ کیا آپ کو یاد نہیں کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا: رفع القلم اھ ) حدیث ابو قتادہ کی تخریج حاکم نے مستدرک میں، حدیث ابو ہریرہ کی تخریج بزار نے مسند میں اور حدیث ثوبان و شداد کی تخریج طبرانی نے مسند الشامیین میں کی ہے۔
The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the afflicted (insane) until he recovers, and from the child until he reaches puberty. Narrated from Aisha, Ali, Abu Qatada, Thawban, and Shaddad ibn Aws. Authentication by Abu Dawood, Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, Hakim, etc. The chain includes Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman, teacher of Abu Hanifa, who is considered trustworthy by Nasa'i and Yahya ibn Ma'in. The best chain is via Abu Dawood.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a citation of the famous hadith 'رفع القلم عن ثلاث' (the pen is lifted from three) which is the foundational proof for the legal incapacity of the sleeper, the insane, and the child. The author first states that this hadith is narrated from six Companions: Aisha, Ali, Abu Qatada, Thawban, Shaddad ibn Aws, and also from Abu Hurayra (mentioned later). He then provides the wording from Aisha's narration as recorded by Abu Dawood, Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, and Hakim: the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the afflicted (mentally ill) until he recovers, and from the child until he reaches puberty.' The author discusses the chain of Aisha's narration, noting that it includes Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman, the teacher of Imam Abu Hanifa, whom some scholars criticized but others like Nasa'i and Yahya ibn Ma'in declared trustworthy. He then cites a different, stronger chain from Ibn Abbas via Ali: Ali ibn Abi Talib encountered a insane woman who had committed adultery, and Umar ordered her stoning. Ali reminded him of the hadith about the three from whom the pen is lifted, and Umar accepted and released her. This version is recorded by Abu Dawood. The author concludes by noting the sources for the other Companions' narrations: Hakim recorded Abu Qatada's, Bazzar recorded Abu Hurayra's, and Tabarani recorded Thawban's and Shaddad's.

Key Terms
رفع القلم (raf' al-qalam): Removal of legal accountability (taklif) for actions, meaning no sin or obligation is recorded.
مبتلى (mubtala): One afflicted with mental disorder or insanity that removes reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sleeper, the insane, the child
B) The sick, the traveler, the child
C) The insane, the woman, the child
D) The sleeper, the elderly, the child

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'رفع القلم عن ثلاث' is a foundational principle in Hanafi fiqh establishing that the sleeper, the insane, and the child are not religiously accountable, though civil liability may still apply.

Liability of Minors and Insane Persons for Destruction (Itlaf)
Ruling that minors and insane persons are liable for property they destroy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability of minors and insane persons for property destruction and explain the legal reasoning (qiyas) used.

Core Idea
Civil liability does not require intent—even children and the insane must compensate for destruction they cause.

A minor or insane person who destroys another's property is liable to pay compensation, even though they are not sinning. This principle rests on the objective fact of destruction, not on intent. The text illustrates this with the analogy of a sleeping person who rolls over and breaks something—he too must compensate despite lacking intent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is 'itlaf' (destruction) by a minor or insane person. The ruling is that compensation (daman) is obligatory (wajib) upon them for the sake of the owner's right.
Note that the ruling applies even though the perpetrator lacks religious accountability (taklif).
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is qiyas: the text compares the case of the child/insane to the case of a sleeping person who causes destruction, and to a leaning wall that falls. The common factor is that liability does not depend on intent.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) because the illa is apparent.
3
Trace the qiyas components
Identify the asl (original case: sleeper on property), hukm al-asl (liable), far' (child/insane), and illa (destruction without intent). The illa is extracted via tanqih al-manat: liability is not dependent on qasd.
The Hanafi position holds the illa is 'destruction' itself, making it a jaliyyah illa.
4
Note the practical consequence
The thamarah is that the child or insane person must pay compensation from their own wealth if they have any, or it remains a debt until they can pay.
This ensures the victim's right is protected regardless of the perpetrator's capacity.
5
Evaluate cross-madhhab agreement
This ruling is muttafaq alayh (unanimously agreed upon) across the four schools. The principle that liability for itlaf is objective is not contested.
No ikhtilaf here, so no tarjih needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله و ان اتلفا شيئا .... الخ - اگر بچہ یاد یوانہ نے کسی چیز کو تلف کر دیا تو متلف علیہ کے احیاء حق کی خاطر دونوں پر تاوان لازم
ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اتلاف کا موجب ضمان ہونا قصد پر موقوف نہیں جیسے اگر کوئی نائم کسی چیز پر گر پڑے اور تلف کر دے یا جھکی ہوئی دیوار گر پڑے اور وہ اس پر گواہ قائم کر چکا ہو تو تا وان لا زم ہوتا ہے۔
If a child or an insane person destroys something, then for the sake of the right of the one whose property is destroyed, compensation is obligatory upon both. Because liability for destruction is not dependent on intent, just as if a sleeper falls on something and destroys it, or a leaning wall falls and destroys, and he had already established a witness, then compensation is obligatory.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that if a child or an insane person causes destruction (itlaf) to someone's property, they are liable to pay compensation (daman). The reason given is that liability for destruction is not based on intention (qasd) but on the fact of destruction itself. The author provides analogies: if a sleeping person rolls over and breaks something, he must pay compensation even though he had no intent. Similarly, if a leaning wall collapses and destroys property, the owner is liable if he failed to demolish it after being warned (the analogy of a leaning wall with a witness). The key principle: civil liability for destruction is objective; it does not require the capacity for intent. Thus, the child and insane person, despite lacking legal capacity for religious accountability, are still liable for damages in civil law.

Key Terms
اتلاف (itlaf): Causing destruction or damage to another's property.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because liability for destruction does not require intent
C) Because the guardian is always responsible
D) Because it is a form of discipline

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, civil liability for property destruction is objective and applies even to minors and the insane, ensuring that victims are compensated regardless of the perpetrator's intent.

The Slave's Confession: Validity and Enforcement
Distinction between financial and hudud/qisas confessions of a slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a slave's confession and distinguish between financial and hudud/qisas confessions regarding enforcement.

Core Idea
A slave's confession is valid but suspended if it affects the master's property; immediate for hudud/qisas.

A slave's legal capacity (ahliyyah) exists, but an impediment (man‘) — the master's property rights — may delay enforcement. This passage from al-Hidayah explains the distinction between financial confessions (suspended until freedom) and confessions involving hadd or qisas (effective immediately). Understanding this distinction is key to applying the concept of impediments in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a slave's confession (iqrar). The ruling: valid (nāfidh) in his own right but not against the master. Determine the two categories: financial and hudud/qisas.
The text explicitly says: 'غلام کا اقرار اس کے اپنے حق میں نافذ ہے نہ کہ مولیٰ کے حق میں'
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'لا يملك العبد والمكاتب شيئا الا الطلاق' (The slave and the mukatab own nothing except divorce). This is a hadith ahad, zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalalah for the Hanafi position.
The hadith is used to prove the slave's capacity for divorce, analogically extended to hudud/qisas.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows the slave owns nothing financial, but his divorce (a personal act) is valid. By analogy, his confession for hudud/qisas, which involve personal liability, is also valid immediately. Financial confessions are suspended because they would destroy the master's property.
The key: 'لا يملك' negates ownership but not capacity for personal acts like divorce or confession for bodily punishments.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Shafi'i scholars hold that a slave's confession is entirely invalid because he lacks full capacity. The Hanafi school maintains validity with suspension, using the hadith and the principle that the slave is originally free in matters of blood (dimā').
The ikhtilaf is methodological: Hanafi uses istihsan to prioritize the slave's capacity; Shafi'i may stick to qiyas on missing ownership.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi position is that financial confessions bind after freedom; hudud/qisas confessions bind immediately. This is the relied-upon ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah.
The text states 'وان اقر بحد او قصاص لزمه فى الحال' (if he confesses to hadd or qisas, it binds him immediately).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غلام کا اقرار اس کے اپنے حق میں نافذ ہے نہ کہ مولیٰ کے حق میں
قال فاما العبد فاقراره نافذ في حق نفسه لقيام اهليته غير نافذ في حق مولاه رعاية لجانبه لان نفاذه لا يعرى عن تعلق الدين برقبته او كسبه و کل دلک اتلاف ماله قال فان اقر بمال لزمه بعد الحرية لوجود الاهلية وزوال المانع ولا يلزمه فى الحال لقيام المانع وان اقر بحد او قصاص نزمه فى الحال لانه مبقى على اصل الحرية فى حق الدم حتى لا يصح اقرار المولى عليه بذلك و ينقذ طلاقه لما روينا ولقوله عليه السلام لا يملك العبد والمكاتب شيئا الا الطلاق ولانه عارف بوجه المصلحة فيه فكان اهلا وليس فيه ابطال ملک المولى ولا تفويت منافعه فينفذ والله اعلم
ترجمہ بہر حال غلام سو اس کا اقرار نا فذ ہے خود اس کے حق میں، قیام اہلیت کی وجہ سے نافذ نہیں ہے اس کے آقا کے حق میں۔ اس کی جانب کی رعایت کیلئے کیونکہ اس کا نفاذ خالی نہیں قرض متعلق ہونے سے اس کی گردن یا کمائی کے ساتھ اور یہ سب مال آقا کا اتلاف ہے۔ پس اگر اس نے کسی مال کا اقرار کیا تو وہ اس کو آزادی کے بعد لازم ہوگا۔ وجود اہلیت و زوال مانع کی وجہ سے اور فی الحال لازم نہ ہوگا قیام مانع کی وجہ سے اور اگر حد یا قصاص کا اقرار کیا تو فی الحال لازم نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ خون کے حق میں اصلی آزادی پر باقی رکھا گیا ہے یہاں تک کہ اس پر آقا کا اقرار حد و قصاص صحیح نہیں اور اس کی طلاق نافذ ہو جائیگی۔ بدلیل حدیث مذکور اور نبی علیہ السلام کے اس ارشاد کی وجہ سے کہ غلام اور مکاتب کسی چیز کے مالک نہیں سوائے طلاق کے اور اسلئے کہ غلام طلاق میں مصالحت کو پہچانتا ہے تو وہ اس کا اہل ہے اور اس میں نہ ملک آقا کا ابطال ہے اور نہ اس کے منافع کو فوت کرتا ہے تو یہ نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ تشریح قوله فاما العبد.... الخ - قوله سابق والصبي والمجنون لا يصح ان پر معطوف ہے مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر غلام کسی چیز کا اقرار کرے تو وہ خود اس کے حق میں نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ پس اگر اس نے یہ اقرار کیا کہ میں نے زید کا ہزار روپیہ کا مال تلف کر دیا تو غلام آزادی کے بعد ماخوذ ہوگا اور حق آقا کی وجہ سے فی الحال ماخوذ نہ ہوگا۔ جائین کی رعایت اسی میں ہے کیونکہ غلام کے اقرار کا نافذ ہونا اس کے رقبہ یا کمائی کے ساتھ قرضہ کے متعلق ہونے سے خالی نہیں ہے اور یہ بہر صورت مال آقا کا اختلاف ہے اور آزادی کے بعد اسلئے ماخوذ ہوگا کہ اس میں اقرار کی اہلیت موجود ہے اور امر مانع یعنی حق آقا کی رعایت زائل ہو چکی ۔
قوله و ان اقر بحد ... الخ - اور اگر غلام نے حد یا قصاص کا اقرار کیا تو اس میں فی الحال ماخوذ ہوگا کیونکہ حد اور قصاص کے حق میں غلام اپنی اصلی آزادی پر باقی رکھا گیا ہے۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ حد و قصاص خواص آدمیت میں سے ہیں اور غلام آدمی ہونے کی حیثیت سے مملوک نہیں ہوتا ۔ بلکہ مال ہونے کی حیثیت سے مملوک ہوتا ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر آقا اپنے غلام پر حد یا قصاص کا اقرار کرے تو صحیح نہیں ہوتا۔ سوال اقرار حد و قصاص کے نفاذ میں بھی تو حق آقا کا بطلان ہے۔
The confession of a slave is valid in his own right but not in the right of his master, out of consideration for the master's side. Because its enforcement would necessarily involve a debt attaching to the slave's person or earnings, and that is destruction of the master's property. So if he confesses to a financial obligation, it binds him after freedom (due to existence of capacity and removal of the impediment) and does not bind him immediately (due to the impediment). If he confesses to a hadd or qisas, it binds him immediately because he is considered to be originally free in matters of blood, so much so that the master's confession regarding hadd or qisas is not valid. And his divorce is effective based on what we narrated and because the Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'The slave and the mukatab own nothing except divorce.' And because he recognizes the benefit in it, so he is capable; and there is no annulment of the master's ownership or loss of his benefits, so it takes effect.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage deals with the legal capacity of a slave to make a confession (iqrar). The author states the principle: a slave's confession is valid (nāfidh) in his own right but not against his master. The reason given: if the confession is enforced, a debt would attach to the slave's person (raqaba) or earnings (kasb), which would ultimately result in loss to the master's property, as the slave and his earnings belong to the master. Therefore, out of consideration for the master's right, the confession does not bind the slave immediately. However, the confession is not void; it is suspended (mawqūf). The slave's own capacity (ahliyyah) exists, but there is an impediment (man‘) – the master's right. Upon emancipation, the impediment is removed, so the confession becomes binding on the former slave. For hudud (fixed criminal punishments) and qisas (retaliation), the ruling is different: the confession binds immediately. This is because, in matters of blood (dimā'), the slave is treated as originally free; his body is not considered property in this context. Hence, the master cannot make a confession regarding hadd or qisas against the slave. The slave's own confession is effective at once, because the right involved is a right of Allah (for hudud) or a personal right (for qisas) that does not involve the master's property. The passage also notes that the slave's divorce is valid, citing the hadith: 'The slave and the mukatab own nothing except divorce.' The rationale: a slave recognizes the benefit of divorce, and it does not destroy the master's ownership or benefits, so it takes effect. The author further clarifies that the slave's confession for financial obligations is binding after freedom, not immediately, because the impediment (master's right) ceases. But for hadd/qisas, the impediment does not exist in the same way, so it binds immediately.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): Confession or admission of a right or liability against oneself.
حرية (hurriyyah): Freedom; the status that removes the impediment (man‘) for the slave's financial confession to become enforceable.
مانع (mani'): Impediment; here, the master's property right that prevents immediate enforcement of the slave's financial confession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a slave's confession for a financial debt become binding?
A) Immediately upon confession
B) After the master's permission
C) After the slave is freed
D) Never

Key Takeaway
A slave's confession is valid, but financial confessions are suspended until freedom; hudud/qisas confessions bind immediately due to the slave's original freedom in blood matters.

Interdiction Due to Foolishness (Safah) and the Hanafi Dispute
Chapter introduction defining safah and outlining intra-Hanafi disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on interdiction for safah and distinguish between the view of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A safih cannot be interdicted according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn allow it to protect his wealth — the mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn.

This lesson explores the concept of safah (foolishness or wasteful spending) and the differing opinions within the Hanafi school on whether a safih can be legally interdicted. The passage clarifies that the disagreement is narrow; most issues on the chapter are agreed upon, and only three specific matters are disputed. Understanding this dispute is crucial for grasping the school's approach to protecting wealth while respecting adult autonomy.

Guided Path
1
Define safah technically
Identify the linguistic and technical meaning of safah as used by Hanafi jurists. Note that safah specifically refers to irrational, wasteful spending against Shari'ah, not other sins.
Safah is not general sinfulness but financial folly.
2
Understand chapter placement
Explain why this chapter on interdiction for safah is delayed after chapters on celestial causes (minority, insanity). The celestial causes are stronger and agreed upon, while safah is acquired and disputed.
3
Identify the key disagreement
State the core dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa does not allow interdiction of a safih; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow it. Recognize that the mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view.
4
Review the agreed issues
Go through the ten examples listed in the passage where Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn agree. This shows that the difference is limited and that the safih retains many legal capacities.
Agreed issues include manumission, marriage, zakat, hajj, etc.
5
Examine the disputed points
The passage mentions three disputed points; two are given: (1) whether hajr can be imposed at all, (2) whether a boy who reaches puberty in a state of safah can receive his wealth immediately. Note the missing third point.

ایک تو یہ کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک سفیہ پر حجر نہیں ہوسکتا صاحبین کے نزدیک ہوسکتا ہے۔ دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جولڑ کا سفہ کی حالت میں بالغ ہو اور چھپیں برس کو پہنچ جائے تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کا مال اس کے سپر د کردیا جائے گا۔ اگر چہ اس میں آثار رشد ظاہر نہ ہوں اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جب تک آثار رشد ظاہر نہ ہوں۔ اس وقت تک مال نہیں دیا جائے
Chapter of interdiction due to corruption. Translation: Chapter on imposing interdiction due to corruption. His statement: 'Chapter of interdiction... etc.' - The reason for delaying this chapter is that the previous causes of interdiction were celestial (divinely ordained), while here the cause is acquired by the servant. Celestial matters are stronger in effect, so they are more appropriate for precedence. Also because the interdiction mentioned in the previous chapter is agreed upon, while the interdiction here is disputed, and the agreed upon deserves precedence. The statement of al-Fadan (?): In 'Inayah' and 'Binayah' etc., it is said that by 'corruption' here is meant 'safah' (foolishness). In 'Ahkam al-Quran', safah originally means lightness. It is said: 'The wind made the tree bend.' And from it is the poet's saying: 'They walked as if swaying spears whose tops the gentle winds made bend.' And another saying: 'We fear that our dreams may become foolish, so they burden time along with the burdened.' ... The book of interdiction. 262. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume 12. The ignorant person is called safih because he is light of intellect, i.e., deficient in intelligence. So the meaning of ignorance includes every person to whom the word safih applies. Thus safih fi al-din is one who is ignorant in matters of religion, safih fi al-mal is one who is unaware of protecting wealth, and safih fi al-ra'y is one who is deficient in intellect. Children and women are called sufaha' because they have deficiency in intellect and discernment. In short, safah is folly and lightness of mind that afflicts a person due to anger or joy, and despite having intellect, it impels him to act against the Shari'ah and follow desires. In the terminology of jurists, its predominant use is for wasteful spending that is against reason and Shari'ah, but the commission of other sins like drinking wine, fornication, etc., is not included in the technical safah. Allamah Hamawi says that extravagance in spending or spending without purpose is the habit of a safih. Similarly, spending on something that pious intelligent people do not consider a purpose, such as giving money to singers, entertainers, buying expensive flying pigeons, etc. Warning: Author of Nihayah and author of Binayah said that all issues of this chapter are based on the saying of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), not on Imam Abu Hanifa's saying, because Imam Abu Hanifa does not believe in interdiction due to safah. Then the author of Nata'ij wrote that this statement is not correct, because most issues of this chapter are agreed upon by Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. For example: 1. If he manumits a slave, his manumission is effective. 2. If he makes a slave mudabbar, it is valid. 3. If his slave-girl comes with a child and he claims it, his lineage is established, the child is free, and the slave-girl becomes umm walad. 4. If he marries a woman, his marriage is valid, and if he names a mahr, the amount of mahr al-mithl is valid from him. 5. If he divorces her before consummation, half is obligatory. 6. Zakat is taken from the wealth of the safih, and he must spend on his children, wife, and those relatives whose maintenance is obligatory. 7. If he intends the Hajj of Islam, he is not prevented from it. 8. If he intends one Umrah, he is not prevented from it. 9. If he is sick and makes bequests for acts of piety and charity, that is allowed from one-third of his wealth. 10. The sinful person is not placed under interdiction with us if he is sound in managing his wealth. After this it is said that in this chapter, the disputed issues between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn are only three, of which two issues are mentioned here and in the beginning of the chapter in Badayah. One is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the safih cannot be interdicted; according to the Sahibayn, he can. The second issue is that if a boy reaches puberty while in a state of safah and becomes fifteen years old, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa his wealth will be handed over to him even if signs of maturity have not appeared; according to the Sahibayn, as long as signs of maturity have not appeared, the wealth will not be given.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is an intra-madhhab dispute and chapter introduction. It explains why the chapter on interdiction due to corruption (safah) is placed after the previous chapters on natural causes of interdiction: celestial causes are stronger and agreed upon, while this cause is acquired and disputed. The term 'safah' is defined linguistically as lightness, and technically as foolishness or irrationality that leads to wasteful spending. The passage clarifies that safah specifically refers to extravagant spending against reason and Shari'ah, not other sins. After defining the term, the author presents a key intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa does not allow interdiction of a safih, while the Sahibayn do. However, a caution is raised that some later scholars claimed all chapter rulings are based on the Sahibayn, but the author of Nata'ij refutes this by listing ten issues on which Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn agree, such as the validity of manumission, tadbir, lineage, marriage, divorce, zakat, maintenance, hajj, umrah, bequests, and non-interdiction of a sinful person who manages his wealth well. Then the three actual points of disagreement are introduced: (1) whether a safih can be interdicted at all (Abu Hanifa says no, Sahibayn yes), (2) whether a boy who reaches puberty in a state of safah can receive his wealth (Abu Hanifa says yes immediately after 15 years, Sahibayn say only after signs of maturity appear). The text cuts off before mentioning the third point. This passage is crucial for understanding the nuanced positions within the Hanafi school on guardianship and financial capacity.

Key Terms
سفہ (safah): Technical term in fiqh for foolishness leading to irrational and wasteful spending counter to Shari'ah and reason.
حجر (hajr): Legal interdiction preventing a person from disposing of their wealth due to incapacity or irresponsibility.
صاحبین (sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, whose views often concur against Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT among the agreed-upon issues between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the safih?
A) The validity of manumission by the safih.
B) The permissibility of imposing interdiction (hajr) on the safih.
C) The obligation of zakat from the safih's wealth.
D) The validity of hajj performed by the safih.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has a narrow dispute on interdiction for safah: Abu Hanifa rejects it, the Sahibayn allow it, and later practice follows the Sahibayn to protect wealth.

The Legal Definition of Safih (Prodigal) and Its Three Types
Defining the term safih and its categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define safih linguistically and technically, distinguish its three types, and identify what is excluded from the technical term.

Core Idea
Safah is not just wasting money—it includes ignorance in religion and opinion, but technically limited to financial extravagance.

The term safih (prodigal) appears in classical fiqh as a legal category affecting financial capacity. In this passage, the author unpacks the linguistic meaning and then narrows it to the technical usage in Hanafi law. Understanding this definition is crucial before studying the rules of interdiction (hajr).

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic root
The word safih is derived from safah meaning lightness or deficiency of intellect. The passage begins by equating safih with jahil (ignorant) due to intellectual weakness.
2
Categorize the three types
The author distinguishes: safih fi al-din (ignorant in religion), safih fi al-mal (unaware of preserving wealth), and safih fi al-ra'y (deficient in opinion/intellect). This shows the broad linguistic scope.
3
Note the technical restriction
In Hanafi legal terminology, 'safah' is predominantly used for financial extravagance that contradicts reason and Shari'ah. Other major sins (e.g., drinking, adultery) are excluded from this technical term.
4
Apply to examples
Allamah Hamawi gives concrete examples: wasteful spending on maintenance, giving money to entertainers, or buying expensive pigeons. These illustrate the pattern that defines a safih.
5
Understand the legal consequence
The definition sets the foundation for the legal ruling on interdiction (hajr). A person identified as safih may be prevented from managing his wealth, according to the Sahibayn.
The passage is from Kitab al-Hajr, indicating the legal context.

كتاب الحجر جاہل کو فیہ اس لئے کہتے ہیں کہ وہ خفیف اعقل یعنی ناقص العقل ہوتا ہے۔ پس جہل کے معنی ہر اس شخص کو شامل ہیں جن پر لفظ سفیہ کا اطلاق ہو۔ یہاں تک کہ سفیہ فی الدین وہ ہوگا جو دین کے معاملہ میں جاہل ہو اور سفیہ فی المال وہ ہو گا جو مال کی حفاظت سے ناواقف ہو اور سفیہ فی الرأی وہ ہوگا جو ناقص العقل ہو۔ بچوں اور عورتوں کو سفہا ، اس لئے کہا جاتا ہے کہ ان کی عقل و تمیز میں نقصان ہوتا ہے۔ بہر کیف سفہ حماقت اور خفت عقل کو کہتے ہیں جو انسان کو غیظ و غضب یا فرح و مسرت سے لاحق ہوتی ہے اور اس کو عقل قائم ہونے کے با وجود موجب شرع کے خلاف عمل کرنے اور خواہشات کی پیروی کرنے پر آمادہ کرتی ہے عرف فقہا میں اس کا غالب استعمال فضول خرچی کے لئے ہوتا ہے جو عقل و شرع کے خلاف ہو تو اس کے سوا دیگر معاصی کا ارتکاب مثلاً شراب خوری، زنا کاری ، سفاہت مصطلحہ میں داخل نہیں۔ علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کہ نفقہ میں اسراف یا بلا غرض خرچ کرنا سفیہ کی عادت ہے۔ اسی طرح ایسی فرض[؟] میں خرچ کرنا جس کو دیندار عقلاء غرض شمار نہیں کرتے۔ جیسے گویوں[؟]، کھیل تماشا کرنے والے کو پیسہ دینا ، اڑنے والے کبوتروں کو گراں قیمت پر خرید نا وغیرہ۔
The Book of Interdiction. [Someone] is called ignorant (jahil) in it because he is light of intellect, i.e., deficient in intellect. So the meaning of jahl includes every person to whom the word safih applies. Thus safih fi al-din is one who is ignorant in matters of religion; safih fi al-mal is one who is unaware of preserving wealth; and safih fi al-ra'y is one who is deficient in intellect. Children and women are called sufaha' because their intellect and discernment are deficient. In short, safah refers to foolishness and lightness of intellect that befalls a person due to anger or joy, and despite having sound intellect, it prompts him to act against the Shari'ah and follow desires. In the terminology of jurists, its predominant use is for extravagance that is contrary to reason and Shari'ah; other sins such as drinking wine or committing adultery are not included in the technical term safahat. Allamah Hamawi says that it is the habit of a safih to spend wastefully in maintenance or spend without any purpose. Similarly, spending in such [؟] that sensible religious people do not consider as a purpose, like giving money to [؟] entertainers, or buying flying pigeons at a high price, etc.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a definitional exposition. It begins by explaining the term 'safih' linguistically as one who is ignorant (jahil) due to deficiency in intellect. The author then categorizes safih into three types: safih fi al-din (ignorant in religious matters), safih fi al-mal (wasteful with wealth), and safih fi al-ra'y (weak in opinion/intellect). The term is also applied to children and women due to their natural deficiency in intellect. The passage then clarifies that in legal terminology, 'safah' specifically refers to wasteful spending that contradicts reason and Shari'ah. Other major sins (kaba'ir) like drinking alcohol or adultery are not included in this technical term. Finally, it cites Allamah Hamawi's explanation that wasteful spending on useless things (like excessive entertainment or buying expensive pigeons) is characteristic of a safih. This definition sets the foundation for the legal rulings on interdiction (hajr) that follow.

Key Terms
سفیه (safih): A person who is ignorant or foolish, especially in financial matters, but also in religion and opinion.
سفاہت (safahat): Foolishness or extravagance contrary to reason and Shari'ah, specifically in financial waste.
حجر (hajr): Legal interdiction preventing a person from managing his own wealth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT included in the technical definition of safah?
A) Spending money on useless entertainment
B) Ignorance in matters of religion
C) Committing murder
D) Weakness in intellect

Key Takeaway
Safah linguistically covers three domains (religion, wealth, opinion) but technically only financial waste; other sins do not constitute safah in Hanafi law.

Evaluating Attribution: Are All Hajr Rulings from Sahibayn?
Refuting a claim about the basis of the Hajr chapter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the claim that the Hajr chapter is based solely on Sahibayn's view by distinguishing agreed-upon from disputed issues and identifying the actual basis.

Core Idea
Most Hajr rulings are agreed; only one issue is exclusively from Sahibayn.

In this passage, the commentator refutes a claim made by earlier scholars that the entire chapter on interdiction (Hajr) in Al-Hidayah is built upon the views of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rather than Imam Abu Hanifa. By systematically listing points of agreement and isolating the few disputes, he demonstrates that such a broad claim is inaccurate. This lesson will train you to critically assess similar claims in Hanafi legal literature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Claim
First, note the claim being refuted: that all issues in the Hajr chapter are based on Sahibayn's view, not Abu Hanifa's.
2
List the Agreed-Upon Rulings
The passage provides ten examples where Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn agree. List them to see the extent of agreement.
These include freeing slaves, marriage, zakat, etc.
3
Isolate the Disputed Issues
Identify the three specific points where they differ. Two are mentioned early in the chapter, one at the end.
The disputes are about interdiction of a safih, handing over wealth, and judge's interdiction for negligence.
4
Analyze Which Disputes Are Based on Whose View
Notice that in the first two disputes, the author treats Abu Hanifa's view as the principle and Sahibayn's as subordinate. Only the third is presented as Sahibayn's view alone.
5
Conclude on the Claim's Accuracy
The passage concludes the original claim is false. Only the title of the chapter ('Bab al-Hajr li al-Fasad') might be justified by Sahibayn's view.
This illustrates careful attribution in Hanafi scholarship.

Source Text

تنبیہ صاحب نہا یہ اور صاحب بنائیہ نے کہا ہے کہ اس باب کے کل مسائل صاحبین کے قول پر بنی ہیں نہ کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے قول پر ۔ اس پر صاحب نتائج نے لکھا ہے کہ یہ بات درست نہیں اسلئے کہ اس باب کے اکثر مسائل پر امام ابوحنیفہ اور صاحبین کا اتفاق ہے۔ مثلا: ا - ان اعتق عبداً نفذ عتقه - لو دبر عبده جاز - لو جاءت جاريته بولد فادعاه ثبت نسبه منه و كان الولد حرًا والجارية ام ولده -٤- ان تزوج امرأة جاز نكاحها و ان سمي لها مهراً جاز منه مقدار مهر مثلها -۵- لو طلقها قبل الدخول وجب لها النصف ٦ - وتخرج الزكاة من مال السفيه و ينفق على اولاده و زوجته و من تجب نفقته من ذوى ارحامه - ان اراد حجة الاسلام لم يمنع منها - - لو اراد عمرة واحدة لم يمنع منها - -۹- ان مرض واوصى بوصايا فى القرب وابواب الخير جاز ذلک فی ثلث ماله ١٠ - ولا يحجر الفاسق عندنا اذا كان مصلحاً لما له اس کے بعد کہا ہے کہ اس باب میں امام ابوحنیفہ اور صاحبین کے درمیان جو اختلافی مسائل ہیں وہ صرف تین ہیں جن میں سے مسئلے تو یہ اسے اور بدایہ میں باب کے شروع میں مذکور ہیں۔ ایک تو یہ کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک سفیہ پر حجر نہیں ہوسکتا صاحبین کے نزدیک ہوسکتا ہے۔ دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ لڑکا سفہ کی حالت میں بالغ ہو اور چھپیں[؟] برس کو پہنچ جائے تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کا مال اس کے سپرد کردیا جائے گا۔ اگر چہ اس میں آثار رشد ظاہر نہ ہوں اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جب تک آثار رشد ظاہر نہ ہوں۔ اس وقت تک مال نہیں دیا جائے گا اور ایک مسئلہ صرف ہدایہ میں باب کے آخر میں مذکور ہے اور وہ یہ کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک قاضی غفلت کے سبب سے حجر کرے گا۔ پھر پہلے دونوں مسئلوں میں بھی امام ابو حنیفہ کے قول کو ذکر میں اصل قرار دیا ہے اور صاحبین کے قول کو اس کے تابع کیا ہے۔ پس اس باب کا صرف ایک مسئلہ ایسا رہا جو صاحبین کے قول پر مبنی ہے نہ کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے قول پر اور وہ آخری مسئلہ ہے جو صرف ہدایہ میں مذکور ہے۔ پس یہ کہنا صحیح نہیں کہ اس باب کے کل مسائل قول صاحبین پر مبنی ہیں۔ ہاں اگر قائل اس کے بجائے یہ کہتا کہ اس باب کو باب الحجر للفساد کے ساتھ ملقب کرنا صاحبین کے قول پر مبنی ہے نہ کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے قول پر تو یہ ایک درجہ میں صحیح تھا۔
Caution: The author of Nihayah and the author of Binayah have said that all the issues of this chapter are based on the statement of the Sahibayn, not on the statement of Imam Abu Hanifah. Regarding this, the author of Nata'ij wrote that this statement is not correct, because most of the issues of this chapter are agreed upon by Imam Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn. For example: 1. If he frees a slave, his freeing is effective. 2. If he makes a tadbir for his slave, it is valid. 3. If his slave-girl gives birth and he claims the child, the lineage is established from him, and the child is free and the slave-girl is an umm walad. 4. If he marries a woman, his marriage is valid, and if he stipulates a dower for her, the amount of the mahr al-mithl is valid from him. 5. If he divorces her before consummation, half is obligatory for her. 6. Zakat is taken from the wealth of the safih, and he spends on his children, wife, and relatives whose maintenance is obligatory. 7. If he intends to perform Hajjat al-Islam, he is not prevented. 8. If he intends to perform one Umrah, he is not prevented. 9. If he becomes ill and makes bequests for acts of piety, that is valid within his one-third. 10. A sinful person is not interdicted according to us if he is a good manager of his wealth. After this, he said that the disputed issues between Imam Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn in this chapter are only three. Two of these issues are mentioned in the beginning of the chapter in the Badayah. One is that according to Imam Abu Hanifah, a safih cannot be interdicted; according to the Sahibayn, he can. The second issue is that if a boy reaches puberty while in a state of safah and reaches [؟] years, then according to Imam Abu Hanifah, his wealth will be handed over to him, even if signs of maturity are not apparent; according to the Sahibayn, wealth will not be given until signs of maturity are apparent. And one issue is mentioned only at the end of the chapter in the Hidayah: that according to the Sahibayn, the judge will interdict due to negligence. Then, in the first two issues, the author considered the statement of Imam Abu Hanifah as the principle and the statement of the Sahibayn as subordinate. So only one issue remains in this chapter that is based on the statement of the Sahibayn, not on the statement of Imam Abu Hanifah, and that is the last issue mentioned only in the Hidayah. So it is not correct to say that all issues of this chapter are based on the statement of the Sahibayn. But if someone said instead that naming this chapter 'Bab al-Hajr li al-Fasad' is based on the statement of the Sahibayn, not on the statement of Imam Abu Hanifah, that would be correct to some extent.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by the commentator. It begins by noting a caution from the authors of Nihayah and Binayah, who claimed that all rulings in the Hajr chapter of Al-Hidayah are based on the Sahibayn's (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) view, not Abu Hanifa's. The commentator then refutes this by citing the author of Nata'ij, who lists ten examples where Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn agree. These include the validity of freeing slaves, tadbir, claiming lineage, marriage, divorce, zakat, spending on dependents, Hajj, Umrah, bequests, and the non-interdiction of a sinful person who manages his wealth. After this, he identifies only three points of disagreement: (1) interdiction of a safih, (2) handing over wealth to a safih who reaches puberty, and (3) the judge's interdiction due to negligence. He further argues that even in the first two, Abu Hanifa's view is treated as the principle, and only the third is purely based on the Sahibayn. Therefore, the sweeping claim is incorrect, though the title of the chapter might be justified by Sahibayn's view. This demonstrates the importance of careful attribution in Hanafi legal scholarship.

Key Terms
صاحبین (al-Sahibayn): Referring to Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two main disciples of Abu Hanifa.
حجر (hajr): Interdiction; a legal restriction on a person's ability to manage their property due to incapacity (safah, travel, etc.).
سفیه (safih): A spendthrift; one who is wasteful or irresponsible with wealth, leading to potential interdiction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many issues in the Hajr chapter are exclusively based on Sahibayn's view?
A) Ten
B) Three
C) One
D) None

Key Takeaway
Attributing an entire chapter to a single source is often an overgeneralization; careful analysis reveals extensive agreement and limited, specific disputes.

The Ruling of Interdiction on a Prodigal: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on interdiction of a prodigal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions regarding interdiction of a safih, explain the proof of each, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A prodigal is not automatically interdicted; Abu Hanifa views it as a greater harm, while Sahibayn see it as protective.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a critical intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a safih (prodigal) should be placed under legal interdiction (hajr). Understanding this dispute requires analyzing arguments from both sides, including qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference). We will work through the proofs of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and see how the later Hanafi school resolved the conflict.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the legal question: should a safih (prodigal) be interdicted from disposing of his property?
2
Present the Sahibayn's position
Sahibayn argue for interdiction by analogy with a child and by the Quranic verse 'Do not give the foolish your property'.
They claim it is a fortiori (awla) because the safih's waste is actual, not just probable.
3
Present Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa argues against interdiction because the safih is mukhatab (legally addressed) and sane; interdiction is a greater harm than his prodigality.
He uses the analogy with a righteous person (rashid) who is not interdicted.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to objections
The text refutes the Sahibayn's analogies and addresses why a slave is interdicted but not a safih.
Two responses: 'mukhatab' in absolute sense excludes slave; by context, financial mukhatab excludes slave who has no property.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of Sahibayn, as it is more protective and supported by majority of later Hanafis.
Al-Marghinani presents it as the basis for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحجر
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲-
في الحجر دفع ضرر عام كالحجر على المتطيب الجاهل والمفتى الماجن والمكارى المفلس جاز فيما يروى عنه اذ هو دفع ضرر الاعلى بالادنى ولا يصح القياس على منع المال لان الحجر ابلغ منه في العقوبة ولا على الصبى لانه عاجز عن النظر لنفسه وهذا قادر عليه نظر له الشرع مرةً باعطاء آلة القدرة والجرى على خلافه لسوء اختياره ومنع المال مفيد لان غالب السفه فى الهبات والتبرعات والصدقات وذلك يقف على اليد
ترجمہ کیونکہ وہ فضول خرچ ہے اپنے مال میں اس کو اس طور پر خرچ نہیں کرتا جس طور پر عقل چاہتی ہے تو اس کو مجبور کر دیا جائے گا۔اس کی بہتری کیلئے بچہ پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے بلکہ وہ بطریق اولی مجور ہو گا۔ کیونکہ بچہ کے حق میں فضول خرچی کا صرف احتمال ثابت ہے اور سفیہ کے حق میں اس کی حقیقت ثابت ہے۔ اس لئے اس سے مال روک دیا گیا۔ پھر خالی ممانعت مفید نہیں ہے حجر کے بغیر کیونکہ وہ اپنی زبان سے تلف کرے گا اس چیز کو جورو کی گئی ہے اس کے ہاتھ سے، امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ مخاطب اور عاقل ہے تو اس پر حجر نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ راست رو پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور یہ اس لئے ہے کہ اس کی ولایت چھین لینے میں اس کی آدمیت مٹانا اور اس کو جانوروں کیساتھ ملا دینا ہے اور یہ زیادہ نقصان دہ ہے۔ فضول خرچی سے تو اعلیٰ ضرر نہیں اٹھایا جائے گا۔ ادنیٰ ضرر دور کرنے کیلئے یہاں تک کہ اگر مجبور کرنے میں ضرر عام کا دفعیہ ہو۔ جیسے جاہل طبیب، بے پرواہ مفتی اور مفلس مکاری پر حجر کرنا تو یہ جائز ہے اس روایت میں جو امام ابو حلیفہ سے مروی ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ ادنی ضرر کے ذریعہ سے اعلیٰ ضرر کا دفعیہ ہے۔ اور مال روکنے پر قیاس کرنا صحیح نہیں کیونکہ مجبور کرنا اس سے بڑھ کر ہے سزا میں اور نہ بچہ پر قیاس کرنا صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنی بہتری کی فکر سے عاجز ہے اور یہ اس پر قادر ہے جس پر شرع نے آلات قدرت عطاء کر کے نظر شفقت کی ہے اور اس کے خلاف پر چلنا اس کی بد اختیاری کی وجہ سے ہے اور مال کا رو کنا مفید ہے۔ کیونکہ اکثر بے وقوفی ہوں اور صدقوں میں ہوتی ہے اور یہ مال کے قبضہ پر موقوف ہے۔ تشریح قوله لانه مبذر ... الخ - صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سفیہ مذکور اپنے مال میں فضول خرچ ہے کہ مال کو بمنتہائے عقل خرچ نہیں کرتا۔ پس اس کی خیر خواہی کے پیش نظر مجبور کر دیا جائے گا۔ جیسے بچہ کو مجور کیا جاتا ہے۔ بلکہ بچہ کی بہ نسبت سفیہ کو بدرجہ اولی مجبور کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ بچہ کے حق میں تو اسراف اور فضول خرچی کا صرف احتمال ہی ہے اور سفیہ میں یہ بات حقیقتا موجود ہے۔ اسی لیئے اس کو مالی تصرف سے روکا گیا ہے۔ قال الله تعالى ولا تؤتوا السفهاء اموالکم پھر خالی ممانعت حجر کے بغیر بے سود ہے کیونکہ وہ مال کو ہاتھ کے بجائے زبان سے تلف کرے گا۔
قوله ولابي حنيفة ... الخ - امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل کی تشریح یہ ہے کہ سفیہ شخص مخاطب بھی ہے اور عاقل بھی ہے۔ ان میں سے پہلا وصف ( مخاطب ہونا ) اہلیت تصرف کی طرف مشیر ہے۔ اسلئے کہ تکلیف اس کی مقتضی ہے کہ استیفاء پر تمکن حاصل ہوتا کہ موجب تکلیف کے مطابق عمل پیرا ہو سکے۔ اور استیفاء پر ممکن اسی وقت ہو گا۔ جب اموال تک رسائی ہو اور اموال تک رسائی تملیک و تملک کے ذریعہ سے ہوتی ہے۔ دوسرا وصف عاقل ہونا ہے جس کے ذریعہ سے اہلیت تمیز ثابت ہوتی ہے۔ پھر شریعت نے رشد کو جو تملیک و ملک کے اعتبار سے تصرفات کی ایک راہ قرار دیا ہے وہ اس معنی کے لحاظ سے ہے اور یہ معنی شخص رشید کی طرح سفیہ آدمی میں بھی موجود ہیں۔ کیونکہ اس میں اس قدر عقل پائی جاتی ہے جس کی وجہ سے حق تعالیٰ نے اس کو مخاطب کیا ہے۔ اگر بچہ کی طرح وہ بھی بے عقل ہوتا تو ایمان و
شرائع کا مخاطب نہ ہوتا۔ پس جیسے رشد و درستگی کیا تھ تصرف کرنے والا مجور نہیں ہوتا۔ اسی طرح سفیہ بھی مجبور نہ ہوگا۔ ورنہ ظاہر ہے کہ اس کی ولایت چھین لینا گویا اس کو آدمیت سے گرا کر جانوروں کے ساتھ ملا دیتا ہے۔ حالانکہ اس کا ضر ر فضول خرچی کی بہ نسبت نہیں زیادہ ہے تو ادنی ضرر ( تبذیر) کی خاطر اعلی ضرر ( حجر ) کا تحمل نہیں کیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ نعمت مال نعمت زائدہ ہے اور زبان کی بندش کا نہ ہونا نعمت اصلیہ ہے۔ چنانچہ آدمی دیگر حیوانات پر جو فوقیت رکھتا ہے وہ اپنے قولی تصرفات ہی کے اعتبار سے رکھتا ہے۔ قوله حتى لو كان في الحجر .... الخ - ہاں اگر مجبور کرنے میں ضرر عام کا دفعیہ ہوتا ہو۔ مثلاً کوئی جاہل شخص طبیب بن بیٹھایا کوئی بے پرواہ و بے حیا شخص مفتی ہو بیٹا یا کوئی مفلس آدمی جس کے پاس جانور وغیرہ نہیں ہیں ۔ وہ کرایہ پر دینے کا ٹھیکیدار ہو گیا تو ان سب کو مجبور کیا جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ امام ابو حنیفہ سے مروی ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ ادنیٰ ضرر کے ذریعہ سے اعلی ضرر کا دفعیہ ہے۔ تنبیه امام ابو حنیفہ کی طرف سے صاحب ہدایہ کی پیش کردہ دلیل انه مخاطب عاقل اھ پر یہ اشکال ہوتا ہے کہ یہ دلیل غلام سے ٹوٹ جاتی ہے کہ غلام بھی مخاطب اور عاقل ہے اس کے باوجود اس پر حجر ہوتا ہے۔ اس کا جواب دو طرح پر ہے۔ ایک یہ کہ یہاں لفظ مخاطب مطلق ہے اور مطلق اپنے فرد کامل کی طرف منصرف ہوتا ہے۔ اور غلام کامل مخاطب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس سے بہت سے مالی خطابات جیسے زکوۃ، صدقہ فطر ، اضحیہ کفارات مالیہ اور بعض خطابات فیہ مالیہ جیسے جی نماز جمعہ نماز عیدین شہادات وغیرہ ساقط ہیں۔
دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہاں مخاطب سے مراد بدلالت محل کلام وہ ہے جو تصرفات مالیہ کا مخاطب ہو۔ کیونکہ گفتگو نعمر فات مالیہ ہی سے حجز کے بارے میں ہے۔ جیسے بیع و شراء، ببات وصدقات وغیرہ ۔ اس صورت میں قول مذکور انه مخاطب غلام کو شامل ہی نہیں اسلئے کہ غلام کا کوئی مال نہیں ہوتا ۔ قوله ولا يصح القياس .... الخ - سائین کے قیاس ولهذا منع عنه المال کا جواب ہے کہ سفیہ پر خنجر کے جواز کوشع مال کے جواز پر قیاس کرنا صحیح نہیں اسلئے کہ منع مال تو بطریق عقوبت اور سزا کے طور پر ہے۔ تا کہ اس کی فضول خرچی پر زجر ہو اور منہ مال کی بہ نسبت مجبور کرنے میں عقوبت زیادہ ہے تو اقوی کو اضعف پر قیاس کرنا صحیح نہ ہوگا۔
اور ان کے دوسرے قیاس اعتباراً بالصبی کا جواب یہ ہے کہ سفیہ کو نبی پر قیاس کرنا بھی صحیح نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ صبی کو اپنے معاملہ میں بہتری کی فکر کرنے کی لیاقت نہیں ہے اور سفیہ کو یہ قدرت حاصل ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کو آزادی و عقل اور بلوغ دیا گیا ہے۔ لیکن وہ اپنی بد اختیاری سے اس کے خلاف راہ چلتا ہے تو یہ قادر کو عاجز پر قیاس کرنا ہوا جو فاسد ہے۔ قوله و منع المال مفيد ... الخ - یہ صاحبین کے قول ثم هو لا يفيد بدون الحجر کا جواب ہے کہ مال سے روک دینا حجر کے بغیر بھی مفید ہے۔ کیونکہ اکثر بیوقوفیاں تبرعات اور صدقات میں ہوتی ہیں اور یہ مال کے قبضہ پر موقوف ہے۔ جب اس کے قبضہ میں کچھ نہ ہو تو وہ کچھ نہیں کر سکتا۔
فائدہ امام ابو حنیفہ کی نفلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے سامنے حضرت حبان بن منقذ کا تذکرہ ہوا جو اکثر اوقات خرید و فروخت میں دھوکا کھا جاتے تھے تو آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا کہ تو خرید کے بعد یہ کہہ دیا کر لا خلابتہ اس میں دھوکا نہیں۔ (صحیحین ابن عمر )
Chapter of Interdiction. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah volume 12. In interdiction for repelling general harm, like interdiction on the ignorant physician, the immoral mufti, and the bankrupt transporter, it is permissible in what is narrated from him, because it is repelling greater harm with lesser. And analogy on prohibition of property is not correct, because interdiction is more severe in punishment. And not on the child, because he is incapable of looking after himself, while this one (the prodigal) is capable. The Shari'ah looked after him once by giving him the tools of capability, and his going against it is due to his bad choice. And prohibition of property is beneficial, because most foolishness is in gifts, donations, and charities, and that depends on possession. Translation: Because he is a prodigal in his property, he does not spend it in the way that reason requires, so he will be interdicted. For his benefit, analogizing to the child, rather a fortiori, because for the child only probability of waste exists, while for the prodigal it is actual. Hence his property was prevented. Then mere prohibition without interdiction is not beneficial, because he will waste with his tongue what is prevented from his hand. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that he is addressed (mukhatab) and sane, so he will not be interdicted, analogizing to the righteous person. This is because removing his guardianship destroys his humanity and likens him to animals, and this is greater harm. Greater harm is not endured for lesser harm. However, if in interdiction there is repelling of general harm, like interdiction on the ignorant physician, the careless mufti, and the bankrupt renter, then it is permissible in that narration from Abu Hanifa, because it is repelling greater harm with lesser. And analogy on prohibiting property is not correct because interdiction is more severe in punishment, and analogy on the child is not correct because he is incapable of looking after his own benefit, while this one is capable. The Shari'ah looked after him once by giving him the tools of capability, and his going against it is due to his bad choice. And prohibition of property is beneficial because most foolishness is in donations and charities, and that depends on possession. Explanation of his statement 'Because he is a prodigal...' - The proof of the Sahibayn is that this prodigal wastes his property, not spending it according to the extent of reason. So for his well-being, he will be interdicted, like a child is interdicted. Rather, the prodigal is more deserving, because for the child there is only probability of waste, while for the prodigal it is actual. Hence his financial transactions are prevented. Allah Almighty said: 'And do not give the foolish your property.' Then mere prohibition without interdiction is useless because he will waste with his tongue. His statement 'And Abu Hanifa...' - The explanation of Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the prodigal person is both addressed (mukhatab) and sane. The first attribute indicates capacity for transactions, because taklif requires ability to act accordingly, which only occurs when he has access to property through ownership. The second attribute indicates capacity of discernment. The Shari'ah has designated sound judgment (rushd) as a path for transactions based on ownership, and this meaning exists in the prodigal as in the righteous person. If he were foolish like a child, he would not be addressed for faith and legal obligations. So just as a righteous person is not interdicted, the prodigal too will not be interdicted. Otherwise, removing his guardianship degrades him from humanity to animals, and his harm is greater than waste. So greater harm (interdiction) is not borne for lesser harm (waste). This is because wealth is a superadded blessing, while freedom of speech is an original blessing. Man's superiority over animals is through his verbal transactions. His statement 'Until if in interdiction...' - Yes, if interdiction repels general harm, e.g. an ignorant person becomes a physician, a shameless person becomes a mufti, or a bankrupt person becomes a transporter, then all will be interdicted, as narrated from Abu Hanifa, because it repels greater harm with lesser. Note: The proof presented by the author of Hidayah from Abu Hanifa 'he is mukhatab and sane' is objected: that it is refuted by a slave, who is also mukhatab and sane yet is interdicted. The answer is twofold: First, the word 'mukhatab' is absolute and absolute tends to its complete individual; and a slave is not a complete mukhatab because many financial addresses like zakat, fitrah, udhiyah, financial expiations, and some mixed addresses like Jumu'ah, Eid prayers, testimony, etc. are dropped from him. Second answer: By the context, 'mukhatab' here means one addressed for financial transactions, because the discussion is about interdiction concerning financial matters like sale, purchase, gifts, charities. In that case, the statement 'he is mukhatab' does not include a slave because a slave has no property. His statement 'And analogy is not correct...' - This is an answer to the Sahibayn's analogy: The permissibility of interdiction on the prodigal cannot be analogized to the permissibility of prohibiting property, because prohibition of property is by way of punishment to deter waste, while interdiction is a greater punishment; so the stronger cannot be analogized to the weaker. And their other analogy with the child is also invalid, because the child lacks the ability to look after his own interest, while the prodigal has that ability, having been given freedom, intelligence, and puberty; but he chooses the opposite path through his bad choice. So this is analogizing the capable to the incapable, which is invalid. His statement 'And prohibition of property is beneficial...' - This is an answer to the Sahibayn's statement 'then it is not beneficial without interdiction': that prohibition of property is beneficial even without interdiction, because most foolishness occurs in donations and charities, and these depend on possession. When he has nothing in his possession, he cannot do anything. Benefit: Imam Abu Hanifa's additional proof: The story of Habban ibn Munqidh was mentioned before the Prophet (peace be upon him), who was often cheated in transactions. The Prophet said, 'When you buy, say: La khilabah (no cheating).' (Sahihayn from Ibn Umar)
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal interdiction (hajr) of a prodigal person (safih) who irrationally wastes his wealth. The two positions are those of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The passage begins by stating the general principle that interdiction to repel general harm is permissible, even according to Abu Hanifa, in cases like an ignorant physician or corrupt mufti. Then it dives into the core dispute. The Sahibayn argue that the safih should be interdicted for his own benefit, drawing an analogy (qiyas) with a minor child, and even a fortiori (bi-tariq al-awla) because the child only potentially wastes while the safih actually does. They also cite the Quranic verse 'Do not give the foolish your property' (4:5), interpreting it as a basis for interdiction. They claim that mere prohibition of property without formal interdiction is useless because the safih can waste through verbal declarations (e.g., gifts, sales) even if his physical possession is restricted. Imam Abu Hanifa counters that the safih is mukhatab (legally addressed) and sane ('aqil), which grants him full capacity for transactions. Interdiction would strip him of his guardianship (wilayah), effectively dehumanizing him and likening him to animals, which is a greater harm than his prodigality. He argues that the greater harm (removing human dignity) cannot be borne for the lesser harm (waste of wealth). He rejects the analogy with a child because a child lacks capacity while the safih possesses it. He also refutes the analogy with prohibiting property, as interdiction is a more severe punishment and cannot be analogized from a lighter measure. He defends that prohibiting property alone is sufficient because most wasteful acts are in donations and charities, which require possession; if the safih's property is withheld, he cannot squander it. The passage then addresses an objection: if a slave is also mukhatab and sane yet is interdicted, why not the safih? The commentary provides two responses: first, 'mukhatab' in absolute terms refers to the perfect individual, and a slave is not perfectly addressed because many obligations fall from him; second, by context, the discussion is about financial transactions, and a slave has no property, so he is not included. Finally, a supporting proof from the Prophet's treatment of Habban ibn Munqidh is mentioned: instead of interdiction, the Prophet advised him to stipulate no cheating in transactions, showing that the sunna does not require interdiction for those who are mentally capable despite being cheated frequently. Thus, Abu Hanifa's position is that interdiction is not the default for a safih; it is only allowed when there is public harm, as an exception. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, however, is that of the Sahibayn, which favors interdiction to protect the safih's wealth.

Key Terms
سفيه (safih): A person who is prodigal, wastes his wealth irrationally without sound judgment.
حجر (hajr): Legal interdiction preventing a person from disposing of his property.
مخاطب (mukhatab): One who is addressed by the divine law (mukallaf), having legal capacity for obligations and transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is a prodigal (safih) not placed under interdiction?
A) Because he is a slave
B) Because he is mukhatab and sane
C) Because he is a minor
D) Because his wealth is protected by a guardian

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school ultimately adopts the Sahibayn's position, making interdiction of a safih the operative ruling, despite Abu Hanifa's strong counter-arguments.

Interdiction of the Squanderer: Abu Hanifa vs the Two Disciples
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hajr of safih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on interdiction of a squanderer, explain the proof of each side, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
A rational adult squanderer is not automatically interdicted; the Hanafi fatwa now allows interdiction per the Sahibayn.

This lesson presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: should a competent adult who wastes his wealth (safih) be placed under legal guardianship (hajr)? Imam Abu Hanifa argues against it, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, argue for it. Understanding their proofs and the eventual tarjih is essential for grasping how the Hanafi school resolves internal differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Recognize that the ruling concerns a safih: a free, rational adult who mismanages his money. The question is whether a qadi can interdict him (restrict his financial capacity).
The safih is not a minor or insane; he is legally competent.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa says no interdiction because the safih is a mukhatab (responsible person). The harm of interdiction (loss of freedom) outweighs wastefulness. He cites the hadith of Habban ibn Munqidh.
The hadith shows the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not interdict a man frequently deceived in trade.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that interdiction is permissible. Their evidence is Quran 2:282, which gives a guardian authority over a squanderer.
They also use qiyas: analogy to preventing waste by prohibiting access to property, and analogy to minors.
4
Analyse Abu Hanifa's responses
The text refutes the Sahibayn's analogies: (1) interdiction is a greater harm than prohibition of property, so the analogy fails; (2) a safih has capacity unlike a minor. Also addresses an objection about slaves by distinguishing perfect and imperfect responsibility.
The commentary explains two ways to counter the slave objection.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Despite Abu Hanifa's reasoning, the later scholars (mutakhkhirin) preferred the Sahibayn's view. Durr al-Mukhtar states the fatwa is on their position.
This means in practice, a qadi can appoint a guardian for a squanderer.

كتاب الحجر
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲ شرائع کا مخاطب نہ ہوتا۔ پس جیسے رشد و درستگی کیا تھ تصرف کرنے والا مجور نہیں ہوتا۔ اسی طرح سفیہ بھی مجبور نہ ہوگا۔ ورنہ ظاہر ہے کہ اس کی ولایت چھین لینا گویا اس کو آدمیت سے گرا کر جانوروں کے ساتھ ملا دیتا ہے۔ حالانکہ اس کا ضر ر فضول خرچی کی بہ نسبت نہیں زیادہ ہے تو ادنی ضرر ( تبذیر) کی خاطر اعلی ضرر ( حجر ) کا تحمل نہیں کیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ نعمت مال نعمت زائدہ ہے اور زبان کی بندش کا نہ ہونا نعمت اصلیہ ہے۔ چنانچہ آدمی دیگر حیوانات پر جو فوقیت رکھتا ہے وہ اپنے قولی تصرفات ہی کے اعتبار سے رکھتا ہے۔ قوله حتى لو كان في الحجر .... الخ - ہاں اگر مجبور کرنے میں ضرر عام کا دفعیہ ہوتا ہو۔ مثلاً کوئی جاہل شخص طبیب بن بیٹھایا کوئی بے پرواہ و بے حیا شخص مفتی ہو بیٹا یا کوئی مفلس آدمی جس کے پاس جانور وغیرہ نہیں ہیں ۔ وہ کرایہ پر دینے کا ٹھیکیدار ہو گیا تو ان سب کو مجبور کیا جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ امام ابو حنیفہ سے مروی ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ ادنیٰ ضرر کے ذریعہ سے اعلی ضرر کا دفعیہ ہے۔ تنبیه امام ابو حنیفہ کی طرف سے صاحب ہدایہ کی پیش کردہ دلیل انه مخاطب عاقل اھ پر یہ اشکال ہوتا ہے کہ یہ دلیل غلام سے ٹوٹ جاتی ہے کہ غلام بھی مخاطب اور عاقل ہے اس کے باوجود اس پر حجر ہوتا ہے۔ اس کا جواب دو طرح پر ہے۔ ایک یہ کہ یہاں لفظ مخاطب مطلق ہے اور مطلق اپنے فرد کامل کی طرف منصرف ہوتا ہے۔ اور غلام کامل مخاطب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس سے بہت سے مالی خطابات جیسے زکوۃ، صدقہ فطر ، اضحیہ کفارات مالیہ اور بعض خطابات فیہ مالیہ جیسے جی نماز جمعہ نماز عیدین شہادات وغیرہ ساقط ہیں۔
تو
دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہاں مخاطب سے مراد بدلالت محل کلام وہ ہے جو تصرفات مالیہ کا مخاطب ہو۔ کیونکہ گفتگو نعمر فات مالیہ ہی سے حجز کے بارے میں ہے۔ جیسے بیع و شراء، ببات وصدقات وغیرہ ۔ اس صورت میں قول مذکور انه مخاطب غلام کو شامل ہی نہیں اسلئے کہ غلام کا کوئی مال نہیں ہوتا ۔ قوله ولا يصح القياس .... الخ - سائین کے قیاس ولهذا منع عنه المال کا جواب ہے کہ سفیہ پر خنجر کے جواز کوشع مال کے جواز پر قیاس کرنا صحیح نہیں اسلئے کہ منع مال تو بطریق عقوبت اور سزا کے طور پر ہے۔ تا کہ اس کی فضول خرچی پر زجر ہو اور منہ مال کی بہ نسبت مجبور کرنے میں عقوبت زیادہ ہے تو اقوی کو اضعف پر قیاس کرنا صحیح نہ ہوگا۔
اور ان کے دوسرے قیاس اعتباراً بالصبی کا جواب یہ ہے کہ سفیہ کو نبی پر قیاس کرنا بھی صحیح نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ صبی کو اپنے معاملہ میں بہتری کی فکر کرنے کی لیاقت نہیں ہے اور سفیہ کو یہ قدرت حاصل ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کو آزادی و عقل اور بلوغ دیا گیا ہے۔ لیکن وہ اپنی بد اختیاری سے اس کے خلاف راہ چلتا ہے تو یہ قادر کو عاجز پر قیاس کرنا ہوا جو فاسد ہے۔ قوله و منع المال مفيد ... الخ - یہ صاحبین کے قول ثم هو لا يفيد بدون الحجر کا جواب ہے کہ مال سے روک دینا حجر کے بغیر بھی مفید ہے۔ کیونکہ اکثر بیوقوفیاں تبرعات اور صدقات میں ہوتی ہیں اور یہ مال کے قبضہ پر موقوف ہے۔ جب اس کے قبضہ میں کچھ نہ ہو تو وہ کچھ نہیں کر سکتا۔
فائدہ امام ابو حنیفہ کی نفلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے سامنے حضرت حبان بن منقذ کا تذکرہ ہوا جو اکثر اوقات خرید و فروخت میں دھوکا کھا جاتے تھے تو آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا کہ تو خرید کے بعد یہ کہہ دیا کر لا خلابتہ اس میں دھوکا نہیں۔ (صحیحین ابن عمر )

كتاب الحجر
سائین کی دلیل حق تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے:
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲
فان كان الذى عليه الحق سفيها او ضعيفاً اولا يستطيع ان يمل هو فليملل وليه بالعدل پھر اگر وہ شخص کہ جس پر قرض ہے بے عقل ہے یا ضعیف ہے یا آپ نہیں بتلا سکتا تو بتلا دے کارگزار اس کا انصاف سے۔ اس آیت سے صاف معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ سفیہ پر اس کے ولی کو ولایت حاصل ہے۔ درمختار میں ہے کہ فتویٰ صاحبین کے قول پر ہے۔
Book of Interdiction. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah, Volume 12. The one who is addressed by the law is not compelled. So just as a person of sound judgment and integrity in transactions is not interdicted, similarly a squanderer (safih) will not be interdicted. Otherwise, it is obvious that taking away his authority is like dropping him from humanity and mixing him with animals. While his harm is not greater than wasteful expenditure, so a lesser harm (wastefulness) does not bear a greater harm (interdiction), because the blessing of wealth is a supererogatory blessing, while the absence of restraint on speech is a primary blessing. Accordingly, the superiority man has over other animals is by virtue of his verbal dispositions. His saying: 'until if there is in interdiction...' etc. - Yes, if compelling involves repelling general harm, e.g., an ignorant person becomes a physician, a reckless and shameless person becomes a mufti, or a bankrupt person who has no animals becomes a lessor of something, then all these will be compelled, as is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa, because this is repelling a greater harm through a lesser harm. Note: The evidence presented by the author of Hidayah on behalf of Imam Abu Hanifa, 'he is a rational responsible person', is objected to: that evidence is refuted by the case of a slave, because a slave is also responsible and rational, yet interdiction is applied to him. The answer is in two ways: First, the word 'responsible' here is absolute, and the absolute is directed to its perfect instance, and a slave is not a perfect responsible person because many financial responsibilities like zakat, sadaqat al-fitr, udhiyah, financial expiations, and some responsibilities involving finance like Friday prayer, Eid prayers, testimony, etc., are dropped from him. Second answer: By context, 'responsible' here means one who is addressed regarding financial dispositions, because the talk is about interdiction concerning financial transactions like sale, purchase, gift, charity, etc. In that case, the mentioned statement 'he is responsible' does not include the slave, because the slave has no property. His saying: 'And analogy is not sound...' etc. - The answer to the Sahibayn's analogy 'and for this reason he was prevented from his property' is that analogy of the permissibility of interdiction on a squanderer to the prohibition of property is not correct, because the prohibition of property is by way of punishment and penalty to deter his wastefulness, and compulsion is a greater penalty than prohibition of property, so analogizing the stronger to the weaker is not correct. And the answer to their other analogy, 'by considering the minor', is that analogizing the squanderer to a minor is also not correct, because a minor does not have the capacity to think about his own benefit, while a squanderer has that ability, as he has been given freedom, intellect, and puberty, but he goes against it by his own bad choice; so this is analogizing the capable to the incapable, which is invalid. His saying: 'And prohibiting property is beneficial...' etc. - This is the answer to the Sahibayn's statement 'then it is not beneficial without interdiction' that preventing property is beneficial even without interdiction, because most foolishness occurs in donations and charities, and these depend on possession of property. When he has nothing in his possession, he cannot do anything. Benefit: Imam Abu Hanifa's supererogatory evidence is that in the presence of the Prophet (peace be upon him), mention was made of Habban ibn Munqidh, who was often deceived in buying and selling, so the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When you buy, say: No deception' (Sahihain from Ibn Umar). The evidence of the two disciples is the saying of Allah Most High: 'Then if the one on whom the right is due is a squanderer or weak or cannot dictate himself, then let his guardian dictate with justice.' From this verse it is clear that the guardian has authority over the squanderer. In Durr al-Mukhtar it is said that the fatwa is on the statement of the two disciples.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal interdiction (hajr) of a squanderer (safih). The author of Ashraf al-Hidayah first presents Imam Abu Hanifa's argument that a squanderer, being a rational adult addressed by religious obligations, cannot be interdicted. Abu Hanifa contends that the harm of interdiction (loss of personal freedom) outweighs the harm of wastefulness; the blessing of free speech and action is fundamental, whereas wealth is secondary. He also argues that coercive measures can be taken only when necessary to prevent greater public harm, such as an incompetent physician or unqualified mufti. The text then addresses an objection concerning slaves: slaves are also rational but are interdicted. The commentator provides two responses: (1) the term 'responsible' is absolute and applies most fully to free persons, not slaves who are deficient in certain obligations; (2) by context, 'responsible' refers specifically to financial responsibilities, which a slave does not have since he owns no property. Next, the passage refutes the Sahibayn's analogies. The Sahibayn argue that just as a wasteful person can be prevented from accessing his property, he can be interdicted; but the commentator points out that prohibiting property is a lesser punishment, while interdiction is a greater one, so the analogy fails. Similarly, the analogy to a minor is invalid because a minor lacks capacity, whereas a squanderer is capable. The Sahibayn's claim that preventing property is useless without interdiction is refuted: most wastefulness occurs in donations, which require possession of property, so simply preventing access to wealth can suffice. Imam Abu Hanifa then offers a hadith proof: the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not interdict Habban ibn Munqidh despite his frequent deception in trade; instead, he taught him a protective statement. This shows that the Prophet's approach was education, not interdiction. The Sahibayn counter with the Quranic verse (2:282) that allows a guardian to manage the affairs of a squanderer. The passage concludes by citing Durr al-Mukhtar that the operative fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view, meaning that the relied-upon position permits interdiction of a squanderer.

Key Terms
سفيہ (safīh): A legally competent adult who wastes his wealth foolishly, though he is rational and has reached puberty.
حجر (ḥajr): A legal restriction placed on a person's capacity to conduct financial transactions, imposed by a qadi.
مخاطب (mukhāṭab): One who is addressed by the legal obligations (taklif), i.e., a rational adult. Here, it is used to argue that a safih should not be interdicted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main evidence for the Sahibayn's position that a squanderer can be interdicted?
A) Hadith of Habban ibn Munqidh
B) Quran 2:282
C) Analogy to a slave
D) Common practice of the caliphs

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a rational adult squanderer can be interdicted by a qadi, according to the relied-upon position of the two disciples (Sahibayn), despite Imam Abu Hanifa's objection.

intermediate
8 min
Dispute on the Age for Handing Over Property to a Safih
Presents the intra-Hanafi dispute on when to give property to a safih who reaches puberty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the age for handing over property to a safih and explain the reasoning (ta'dib, athar al-siba, and Quranic condition) behind each view.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa sets 25; the Sahibayn require prudence – a dispute over the cause and duration of interdiction.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on the fate of a person who reaches puberty but remains financially foolish (safih). Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), differ on when his property should be handed over to him and whether his pre-giving transactions are valid. We will explore each side's evidence and reasoning, and discover which view is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their positions
First, note the two opposing views: Abu Hanifa holds that property must be handed over at age 25 unconditionally, and any earlier transaction is valid. The Sahibayn hold that property is not given until prudence (rushd) is shown, and transactions before that are invalid.
The Sahibayn are joined by the three Imams (al-Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad).
2
Understand the cause of dispute
The core difference is the nature of the prevention: Abu Hanifa treats it as a disciplinary measure (ta'dib) that naturally ends at 25; the Sahibayn see the prevention as based on the 'illa (cause) of safah, which persists as long as the person remains foolish, analogous to childhood.
This distinction determines whether a fixed age or a condition (rushd) applies.
3
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn rely on Quran 4:6 which conditions giving property on perceiving prudence, and they use qiyas to childhood: just as a minor is prevented due to lack of judgment, so is a safih in adulthood.
Their evidence is both textual (Quran) and analogical (qiyas).
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa argues that after 25, the disciplinary purpose is no longer served (the person often becomes a grandfather), and the prevention originally due to the effect of childhood (athar al-siba) ceases over time. He also notes that if one becomes prudent then later foolish, property is not withheld, showing the cause is not a new deficiency.
Abu Hanifa uses istihsan (juristic preference) to override the literal application of the verse.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
Later authorities (e.g., Durr al-Mukhtar) state that the fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view. Thus, the practical ruling is that a safih remains interdicted until prudence is shown, and his transactions are void.
Under Abu Hanifa, the safih would have full control at 25 and his earlier transactions would be valid.
