علامات بلوغ
ما العلامة فلان البلوغ بالانزال حقيقة والحبل والاحبال لا يكون الا مع الانزال وكذا الحيض في اوان الحبل فجعل كل ذلك علامة البلوغ
ترجمہ بہر حال علامات سو اس لئے کہ در حقیقت بالغ ہونا انزال سے ہوتا ہے اور حمل کا ہونا یا حاملہ کرنانہیں ہوتا مگر انزال کے ساتھ اور ایسے ہی حیض ہے زمانہ حمل میں ۔ پس ان سب کو بلوغ کی علامت قرار دے دیا گیا عمر کے اعتبار سے مدت بلوغ
وادنى المدة لذلك فى حق الغلام اثنتا عشرة سنة وفى حق الجارية تسع سنين واما السن فلهم العادة الفاشية فى ان البلوغ لا يتأخر فيهما عن هذه المدة وله قوله تعالى حتى يبلغ اشده واشد الصبي ثمانى عشر سنة هكذا قاله ابن عباس وتابعه القُتبى وهذا اقل ما قيل فيه فبنى الحكم عليه للتيقن به غير ان الاناث تشوء هن وادراكهن اسرع فنقصنا في حقهن سنة لاشتمالها على الفصول الاربعة التي يوافق واحد منها المزاج لا محالة
ترجمہ اور اس کیلئے ادنی مدت لڑکے کے حق میں بارہ سال اور لڑکی کے حق میں نو سال ہے۔ رہا سن سوان کی دلیل عادت ظاہرہ ہے اس بارے میں کہ ان دونوں کا بالغ ہونا اس مدت سے متاخر نہیں ہوتا۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل قول باری ہے۔ حتی یبلغ اشدہ اور اشد بی اٹھارہ برس ہے۔ حضرت ابن عباس نے ایسا ہی فرمایا ہے اور قمی نے انہیں کی متابعت کی ہے اور یہ سب سے کم ہے جو اشد کی بابت کہا گیا ہے تو حکم کا مدار بوجہ یقین اس پر رکھا گیا۔ صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ عورتوں کا بڑھنا اور بالغ ہونا بہت جلد ہوتا ہے تو ان کے حق میں ہم نے ایک سال کم کر دیا اس کے چاروں فصلوں پر مشتمل ہونے کی وجہ سے جن میں سے کوئی ایک لامحالہ مزاج کے موافق ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح قوله وادنى المدة .. الخ - لڑکے کے حق میں کمتر مدت جس میں وہ بالغ ہو سکتا ہے بارہ سال ہیں اور لڑکی کے حق میں نو سال ۔ پس اگر وہ اتنی مدت میں بلوغ کا دعوی کریں تو ان کا قول مسموع ہو گا اور ان کے احکام بالغوں کے احکام ہوں گے۔ شرح مجمع میں
Signs of Puberty: What is the sign? Indeed, puberty is in reality by inzal (emission). Pregnancy and causing pregnancy only occur with inzal. Similarly, menstruation occurs at the time of pregnancy. So all of these are made signs of puberty. Translation: In any case, signs are because in reality attaining puberty is through inzal. Pregnancy or causing pregnancy does not occur except with inzal. Similarly, menstruation occurs in the time of pregnancy. So all of these have been declared signs of puberty. Regarding age, the period of puberty: The minimum period for that in the case of a boy is twelve years, and in the case of a girl is nine years. As for the age (of majority), they rely on the widespread custom that puberty does not delay beyond this period. And for him (Imam Abu Hanifa) is the saying of Allah: 'until he reaches his full strength (ashudd)' and the full strength of a boy is eighteen years. Thus said Ibn Abbas, and al-Qutbi followed him. And this is the least that has been said about ashudd, so the ruling is built upon it for certainty. However, females grow and attain it more quickly, so we decreased one year in their case because it encompasses the four seasons, one of which necessarily suits the temperament. Elaboration of his saying 'and the minimum period...': The minimum period in which a boy can become baligh is twelve years, and for a girl nine years. So if they claim puberty within this period, their claim is accepted, and their rulings are the rulings of adults. In Sharh al-Majma.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage provides a two-part ruling: first, reiterating that the essence of puberty is inzal (emission), and other signs (pregnancy, menstruation) are indicators. Second, it establishes the minimum age for claiming puberty: 12 years for a boy and 9 years for a girl. The proof for the age of full maturity (18 for boys, 17 for girls as default) is the Quranic verse 'until he reaches his full strength' (ashuddahu), which Ibn Abbas interpreted as 18 years. This is the minimum age interpreted for 'ashudd', so the ruling is based on it for certainty (al-tayaqqun). For females, one year is subtracted because they mature faster, and the four seasons ensure that one season will match their temperament to bring about puberty. The practical effect: if a child claims puberty at the minimum age, their claim is accepted without requiring proof of signs. The commentary from Sharh al-Majma confirms that at these ages, the child's claim is admissible and they are given adult rulings.

Key Terms
ادنی مدت (adnā muddah): The minimum age at which puberty can be claimed and accepted by the court: 12 years for boys, 9 years for girls.
اشد (ashudd): The age of full strength and maturity; interpreted as 18 years by Ibn Abbas, used as the default age for puberty in Hanafi fiqh when signs are absent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum age at which a girl's claim of puberty is accepted in Hanafi fiqh?
A) 9 years
B) 12 years
C) 15 years
D) 17 years

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a child can claim puberty at 12 (boy) or 9 (girl); without a claim, puberty is presumed at 18 (boy) or 17 (girl) based on the Quranic term 'ashudd'.

Age of Majority (Bulugh) — Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Determines age of majority with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the age of majority according to Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, identify the evidence each side uses, and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Puberty is primarily determined by physical signs; age is a secondary default debated at 18/17 or 15.

This lesson delves into the Hanafi fiqh rules for determining when a person becomes legally responsible (mukallaf). While physical signs like wet dreams and menstruation are primary indicators, the school differs on the default age when these signs are absent. You will explore the Quranic and hadith evidence that led Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Sahibayn) to their respective positions, and learn the practical impact of this difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions on default age
State clearly the age thresholds set by Abu Hanifa (18 for boys, 17 for girls) and by the Sahibayn (15 for both).
These are default ages when no physical signs appear.
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's evidence
Analyze the Quranic verse 'until he reaches ashudd' and Ibn Abbas's interpretation that ashudd means 18 years. Note why girls get one year less.
The verse is from Surah al-An'am, al-Isra', etc.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's evidence
Study the hadith of Ibn Umar (accepted at 15 for battle) and the hadith of Anas (obligations at 15), plus widespread custom.
Both hadith are cited as proof for 15 years.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response
Understand how Abu Hanifa rebuts the hadith: Ibn Umar's hadith is about combat strength, not legal majority; Anas's hadith is weak.
Taj al-Shari'ah adds the precedent of Aisha reaching puberty at 9.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Identify the practical difference in daily life, such as marriage and contracts, and note which view is well-known (mashhur) and which is often adopted later.
The text labels Abu Hanifa's view as well-known, but later practice often uses 15.

Book of Hajj? 278 Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya Volume 2 ... if he reaches that time and does not have a wet dream, he is like a man. Sheikh Abu al-Fadl says: This issue is mentioned in the Book of Agency in two places from Abu Sulayman's narration. One place says: The puberty of a boy is the completion of nineteen years, and the puberty of a girl is the completion of seventeen years. And in another place: That he enters the nineteenth year and she enters the seventeenth year. The described (author) says: This is the well-known saying of Imam Abu Hanifa, and in the Book of Agency, from the narration of Sheikh Abu Hafs, I found the saying agreed upon. Imam Tahawi mentioned in the Book of Siyar from Sharh al-Athar: And Muhammad ibn al-Hasan held for the boy the opinion of Abu Yusuf, and for the girl the opinion of Abu Hanifa. Signs of puberty: What is the sign? Puberty is in reality by emission (inzal). Pregnancy and causing pregnancy only occur with emission, and likewise menstruation at the time of potential pregnancy. So all these are made signs of puberty. Translation: In any case, signs are that in reality maturity occurs by emission, and pregnancy or causing pregnancy does not occur except with emission, and similarly menstruation is at the time of potential pregnancy. So all of these are considered signs of puberty. As for the duration of puberty by age: The minimum period for that regarding a boy is twelve years, and regarding a girl is nine years. As for the age (limit), there is for them (the Sahibayn) the widespread custom that puberty in both does not delay beyond this period. And for him (Abu Hanifa) is the verse: 'Until he reaches his full strength (ashudd)', and the ashudd of a boy is eighteen years; thus said Ibn Abbas, and al-Qutabi followed him. And this is the least said about it, so the ruling is built on it for certainty. However, females grow and their attainment is quicker, so we reduced one year for them because it comprises the four seasons, one of which inevitably suits the temperament. Explanation of 'and the minimum period...': The minimum period in which a boy can become mature is twelve years, and for a girl nine years. So if they claim maturity within this period, their claim is accepted and their rulings are rulings of adults. In Sharh al-Majma': The jurists agree that if a girl of five years or less sees blood, it is not menstruation; and if a girl of nine years or more sees blood, it is menstruation; and for six, seven, eight years, there is disagreement. In al-Kafi, from some authorities, it is narrated that the minimum is eleven years. (Tahatawi). His saying 'As for the age...' is conjuncted to 'as for the sign'. The meaning is: Through age, regarding the fifteen-year period of puberty, the evidence of the Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi'i is the widespread custom that both a boy and a girl do not delay puberty beyond fifteen years. In the Sahihs, it is narrated from Ibn Umar: He said, 'I was presented to the Prophet on the day of Uhud when I was fourteen years old, and he did not accept me and did not consider me mature. And I was presented to him on the day of the Trench when I was fifteen years old, and he accepted me and considered me mature.' Also from Anas: The Messenger of Allah said, 'When a child completes fifteen years, his wealth and his liabilities are recorded, and the prescribed punishments are applied to him.' His saying 'and for him (Abu Hanifa) is the verse...' — Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence is this verse: 'And do not approach the orphan's property except in the best manner until he reaches his full strength (ashudd).' In this, some interpret 'ashudd' as twenty-two years, some as twenty-three, some as twenty-five. According to the author of al-Hidayah, from Ibn Abbas, eighteen years is narrated. Imam Abu Hanifa took this because it is the least of the statements. However, because a girl generally matures quickly, one year was reduced for her, because within a year the four seasons exist, one of which inevitably suits the temperament. Benefit: The response to the hadith of Ibn Umar is that it does not prove the claim because the permission for fighting depends on strength and power for combat, and the permission given at fifteen was for that reason; at that time he had become strong enough for combat, not because the ruling is on puberty or its absence. The narration of al-Hakim from Samura ibn Jundub with the words '...if I wrestled him, I would throw him' indicate that. Question: In the narrations of Bayhaqi and Ibn Hibban, after 'he did not inform me' there is addition 'and he did not consider me mature', and after 'he permitted me' there is addition 'he considered me mature' and Ibn Khuzaymah authenticated this addition. Answer: The meaning of 'he considered me mature' is that he considered me reached the limit of strength for combat. As for the hadith of Anas, the response is that this hadith is not established, so argumentation with it is invalid. Taj al-Shari'ah said: Because it is narrated from Aisha that she reached puberty at nine years, and it is narrated that the Prophet consummated the marriage when she was nine, and it is known that consummation by the Messenger of Allah is only for procreation, which is only realized after puberty, so her puberty is known from that.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf Ul Hadaya deals with the legal age of puberty (bulugh) in Hanafi fiqh. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), with reference also to Imam al-Shafi'i's view. The passage begins by stating that the reality of puberty is through the emission of seminal fluid (inzal) for males, and for females through menstruation (hayd) and pregnancy (haml). These physical signs are considered clear indicators of bulugh. However, when these signs are not present, the jurists resort to age as a secondary criterion. The text gives the minimum age at which a claim of puberty can be accepted: twelve years for a boy and nine years for a girl, based on the fact that physical development rarely occurs before these ages. After this minimum, if a child claims to have experienced the signs, it is accepted. The main dispute concerns the default age of majority when no signs appear. According to the Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi'i, the age is fifteen years for both genders. They rely on widespread custom and the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar, who was not accepted for battle at fourteen but was accepted at fifteen, indicating his majority. They also cite the hadith of Anas that at fifteen, obligations and punishments apply. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, argues that the age is eighteen years for a boy and seventeen for a girl. His primary proof is the Quranic verse 'until he reaches his full strength (ashudd)', and he adopts the interpretation of Ibn Abbas that 'ashudd' is eighteen years. Since girls develop faster, he deducts one year, making it seventeen. He responds to the hadith of Ibn Umar by explaining that the Prophet's acceptance was based on physical strength for fighting, not on legal majority. The report of Anas is deemed weak (ghayr thabit) and thus not acceptable as evidence. The passage concludes with a narration from Aisha that she reached puberty at nine, confirming that the lower age for girls is consistent with early development. Thus, the Hanafi school offers two views: the well-known view (mashhur) of Abu Hanifa at 18/17, and the view of the Sahibayn at 15. In later practice, many Hanafi jurists adopted the Sahibayn's view for practical convenience, but the text here presents Abu Hanifa's as the stronger argument.

Key Terms
بلغوغ (bulugh): Legal puberty: the attainment of physical maturity, marked by seminal emission (inzal) in males, menstruation (hayd) or pregnancy (haml) in females, or by reaching a default age.
أشد (ashudd): Full physical and mental maturity; in this context, interpreted as the age at which a person reaches complete strength and discretion, taken by Abu Hanifa as 18 years for boys.
علامات بلوغ (‘alamāt al-bulūgh): Signs of puberty: (1) wet dream (inzal) for boys, (2) menstruation (hayd) for girls, (3) pregnancy (haml) for girls.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa (رحمه الله), what is the age of majority for a boy who has not shown any signs of puberty?
A) 15 years
B) 18 years
C) 12 years
D) 20 years

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recognizes two default ages for majority: 18/17 (Abu Hanifa) and 15 (Sahibayn), with physical signs always taking precedence.

12 min
Age of Puberty: Hanafi vs. Sahibayn/Shafi‘i
Determining minimum age for puberty and menstruation with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and compare the Hanafi position on the default age of puberty with that of the Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi‘i, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Puberty age is 18 for males (17 females) per Abu Hanifa; 15 per Sahibayn/Shafi‘i — the difference affects legal capacity until 18.

This lesson delves into a classical Hanafi dispute on the maximum age of puberty (sin al-bulugh). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) along with Imam al-Shafi‘i hold that 15 years is the default age of majority for both genders, based on hadith and custom. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, sets it at 18 for males and 17 for females, relying on the Quranic term 'ashudd' and a narration from Ibn ‘Abbas. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for determining when obligations become binding and when one may be subject to penal liability or contractual capacity.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on the age of puberty
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that in the absence of physical signs, a male reaches puberty at 18 years, a female at 17. This is based on the Quranic phrase 'hatta yablugha ashuddahu' (until he reaches his strength) interpreted as beginning at 18.
One year is reduced for females due to earlier physical maturity.
2
Identify the opposing views
The Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi‘i hold that the maximum age of puberty is 15 for both males and females, relying on the widespread custom and the hadith of Ibn ‘Umar and Anas.
This is also the predominant position in the Shafi‘i school.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Abu Hanifa argues that the Quranic 'ashudd' clearly indicates a later age of full strength. The minimum transmitted interpretation of 'ashudd' from Ibn ‘Abbas is 18 years, so Abu Hanifa adopts it for precaution (ihtiyat). For females, he reduces one year because they typically mature faster.
The hadith of ‘A’ishah (puberty at 9) is used as circumstantial evidence for early female maturity, but only as a sign, not the default age.
4
Examine the opposing proofs
The Sahibayn and Shafi‘i cite the hadith of Ibn ‘Umar who was not accepted for battle at 14 but accepted at 15, interpreted as evidence of puberty at 15. They also cite a hadith of Anas that at 15 years obligations are recorded. They argue by widespread custom that most children show signs of puberty by 15.
The Hanafi response interprets the Ibn ‘Umar hadith as about battle strength, not legal puberty. The Anas hadith is declared weak by some critics.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
A person aged 15 is considered fully adult (baligh) according to the Sahibayn/Shafi‘i view, meaning they can marry, be liable for hudud, and transact independently. According to Abu Hanifa, such a person is still a minor until 18 (17 for females) unless physical signs appear, so they cannot incur full criminal liability or manage property without a guardian.
At 18, both views agree on adulthood.

قال عرضت على النبي يوم احد و انا ابن اربع عشرة فلم يقبلنى ولم يرني بلغت وعرضت عليه يوم الخندق وانا ابن خمس عشرة سنة فقبلني وراني انی بلغت
نیز حضرت انسؓ سے مروی ہے:
قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : اذا استكمل المولود خمس عشرة سنة كتب ماله وما عليه و اقيمت عليه الحدود
قوله وله قوله تعالى ...... الخ - امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے:
ولا تقربوا مال اليتيم الا بالتي هي احسن حتى يبلغ اشدہ اس میں اشد سے مراد بعض کے نزدیک بائیس سال کی عمر ہے اور بعض کے نزدیک تئیس سال کی اور بعض کے نزدیک پچیس سال کی، بقول صاحب ہدایہ حضرت ابن عباس سے اٹھارہ سال کی عمر منقول ہے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ نے اس کو لیا ہے کیونکہ یہ اقل الاقوال ہے۔ البتہ لڑکی چونکہ عموما جلد بالغ ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے اس کے حق میں ایک سال کم کر دیا گیا۔ کیونکہ سال کے اندر چاروں فصلیں موجود ہیں۔ جن میں سے کوئی نہ کوئی لا محالہ مزاج کے موافق ہوگی۔ فائدہ اور حدیث ابن عمر کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس سے مدعا ثابت نہیں ہوتا اس لئے کہ اجازت قتال کا حکم، قتال کی طاقت وقوت پر منحصر اور پندرہ سال جو آپ نے اجازت مرحمت فرمائی وہ اسی لئے تھی وہ اس وقت قتال کے لائق طاقتور ہو چکے تھے۔ اس سے پہلے نہیں تھے۔ نہ اس لئے کہ حکم مذکور بلوغ و عدم بلوغ پر ہے۔ حاکم کی روایت سمرہ بن جندب کے الفاظ ولو صارعته لصرعته، قال: فصارعته نہ کہ پر ولو فصرعتہ اس پر دال ہیں۔ سوال بیہقی اور ابن حبان کی روایت میں لم يخبرنی کے بعد ولم یرنی بلغت اور فاجازنی کے بعد رانی قد بلغت کا اضافہ موجود ہے اور ابن خزیمہ نے اس اضافہ کی تصحیح بھی کی ہے۔
جواب .. رانی قد بلغت کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ رانی قد بلغت في القوة حد القتال یعنی پندرہویں سال آپ نے مجھے حد قتال کی قوت میں پایا۔ رہی حدیث انس سو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ حدیث ثابت نہیں پس اس سے احتجاج ساقط ہے۔
قال تاج الشريعة لما روى عن عائشة بلغت على رأس تسع سنين، وروى ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بنى بها حين صار لها تسع سنين، و معلوم ان البناء من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يكون الا للتوالد و التناسل ولا يتحققان الا بعد البلوغ، فعلم بذلك بلوغها -
قوله هكذا قاله ابن عبا.... الخ ليكن يہ بقول علامہ زیلعی غریب ہے۔ نیز بلوغ اشد کے بارے میں جو حضرت ابن عباس سے منقول ہے ہو مابین ثمانی عشرہ ستیہ الی ثلاثین یہ بھی غیر ثابت ہے کیونکہ ابن جریر نے اپنی تفسیر میں اسکو ضعیف قرار دیا ہے اور کہا ہے روى عن ابن عباس من وجه غير مرضى البتہ حافظ ابن حجر نے درایہ میں کہا ہے کہ تفسیر بغوی میں حضرت ابن عباس سے بلا اسناد منقول ہے انه قال: هو ما بين ثماني عشرة سنة الى اربعین اور بظاہر گو یہ بھی ضعیف ہے۔ تاہم الفاظ قرآن سے قریب ہے کیونکہ حق تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے حتی اذا بلغ اشده و بلغ اربعين سنة پس بہت ممکن ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ نے اس روایت ضعیفہ پر اس لئے اعتماد کیا ہو کہ اس باب میں اس سے زیادہ قوی روایت نہیں ہے۔
چنانچہ حافظ بیہقی نے جو حضرت انس سے روایت کی ہے :
اذا استكمل المولود خمس عشرة سنة كتب ماله وما عليه و اقيمت عليه الحدود
یہ بھی ضعیف ہے۔ قاله الحافظ في التلخيص
بہر کیف روایت ابن عباس اختیار کرنے میں احتیاط ہے اس لئے کہ جو شخص اٹھارہ سال کا ہو جائے وہ دونوں روایتوں کے مطابق بالغ قرار پاتا ہے۔ بخلاف اس کے جو پندرہ سال کا ہو کہ وہ صرف روایت انس پر بالغ قرار پاتا ہے نہ کہ روایت ابن عباس پر۔ سوال . اشد کی تفسیر جو عشرین یا ثلاثین یا اربعین سے کی گئی ہے وہ اٹھارہ سال کی بہ نسبت اولی ہونی چاہئے۔ چنانچہ حافظ طبرانی نے معجم اوسط میں حضرت ابن عباس سے روایت کی ہے:
في قوله تعالى حتى اذا بلغ اشده. قال ثلاث وثلثون سنة، وهو الذى رفع علیه عیسی ابن مریم اور تفسیر ابن مردویہ میں حضرت ابن عباس ہی سے روایت ہے:
حتى اذا بلغ اشده. قال: تسعا وثلاثين سنة،
جواب بالکل نہیں۔ اس لئے کہ حضرت انس و ابن عباس کے درمیان جو نزاع ہے وہ مبدا اشد کے بارے میں ہے اور عشرین وغیرہ سے جو تفسیر کی گئی ہے۔ اسمیں اس کو مصداق قرار دیا گیا ہے جس کا حضرت ابن عباس انکار نہیں کرتے۔
فانه يقول : هو من ثماني عشرة الى ثلاثين او اربعين
-
قوله وهذا اقل ما قيل فيه الخ یعنی اشد کے معنی میں جو مقدار میں منقول ہیں وہ مختلف ہیں بعض نے ۲۰ سال، بعض نے ۲۲ سال، بعض نے ۲۵ سال، بعض نے ۳۳ سال بعض نے ۴۰ سال بعض نے ۶۲ سال، ذکر کی ہے۔ ان میں سب سے کم جو مقدار ہے و ۱۸ سال کی ہے جو حضرت ابن عباس کا قول ہے۔ تو حکم بوجہ تیقین اس پر مبنی ہو گا۔ صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ عورتوں کا نشو و نما اور بلوغ بہت جلد ہو جاتا ہے۔ تو ان کے حق میں ایک سال کم کر دیا گیا کیونکہ سال فصول اربعہ (ربیع و خریف صیف وشتا) پر مشتمل ہوتا ہے۔ جن میں سے کوئی ایک فصل لا محالہ مزاج وطبیعت کے موافق ہوگی۔
قوله للتيقن به..... الخ اس پر ایک قومی اشکال ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ صغیر کے زمانہ اشر کو پہنچنے کے بارے میں متیقن مدت تو وہ ہے جو مذکورہ مدتوں میں سب سے اکثر ہے نہ کہ وہ مدت جو ان میں سب سے کم ہے۔ اس لئے کہ جو شخص ان میں سے اکثر مدت کو پہنچ جائے وہ
Book of Interdiction. It states that the jurists agree that if a girl of five years or less sees blood, it is not menstruation. And if a girl of nine years or more sees blood, it is menstruation. And for six, seven, eight years there is disagreement. In al-Kafi, it is narrated from some authorities that the minimum duration is eleven years. (Tahatawi). His statement: 'And as for the age...' etc. is connected to 'And as for the sign...' The meaning is that regarding the age of fifteen years as the term of puberty, the proof of the Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi'i is the widespread custom that both boys and girls do not delay in reaching puberty beyond fifteen years. In the Sahih collections, it is narrated from Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him): He said: 'I was presented before the Prophet on the day of Uhud while I was fourteen years old, and he did not accept me and did not consider me to have reached puberty. And I was presented before him on the day of Khandaq while I was fifteen years old, and he accepted me and considered that I had reached puberty.' Also narrated from Anas (may Allah be pleased with him): The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When the child completes fifteen years, his wealth and his obligations are written, and the legal punishments are established against him.' His statement: 'And for him is the saying of Allah...' etc. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is this verse: 'And do not approach the property of the orphan except in the best manner until he reaches the age of strength (ashudd).' Regarding this, some consider 'ashudd' to mean twenty-two years of age, some twenty-three, some twenty-five. According to the author of al-Hidayah, eighteen years is narrated from Ibn 'Abbas. Imam Abu Hanifa adopted this because it is the minimum of the sayings. However, since girls usually reach puberty early, one year was reduced for them because within the year all four seasons are present, one of which will inevitably suit the temperament. Benefit: The response to the hadith of Ibn 'Umar is that it does not prove the claim because permission for fighting depends on strength and power for fighting, and when he (peace be upon him) granted permission at fifteen years, it was because at that time he had become strong enough for fighting, not before, nor because the aforementioned ruling depends on puberty or its absence. The narration of al-Hakim from Samurah ibn Jundub with the words 'If I had wrestled him, I would have thrown him.' He said: 'So I wrestled him' and not 'and if you threw him' indicate this. Question: In the narration of al-Bayhaqi and Ibn Hibban, after 'he did not inform me' there is an addition of 'and he did not consider me to have reached puberty' and after 'he permitted me' there is 'and he considered that I had reached puberty', and Ibn Khuzaymah authenticated this addition. Answer: The meaning of 'he considered that I had reached puberty' is 'he considered that I had reached the strength to fight' i.e., at fifteen years he found me to have the strength of fighting. As for the hadith of Anas, its response is that this hadith is not established, so argumentation with it falls. Taj al-Shari'ah said: Because it is narrated that 'A'ishah reached puberty at the age of nine, and it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) married her when she became nine years old, and it is known that marriage by the Messenger of Allah is only for procreation and reproduction, and these are not realized except after puberty, so her puberty is known from that. His statement: 'Thus said Ibn 'Abbas...' etc. But according to the saying of 'Allamah Zayla'i, this is strange. Also, regarding 'ashudd', what is narrated from Ibn 'Abbas: 'He is between eighteen years and thirty' is also unestablished because Ibn Jarir in his Tafsir declared it weak and said: 'Narrated from Ibn 'Abbas from an unreliable source.' However, Hafiz Ibn Hajar in al-Dirayah said: In Tafsir al-Baghawi, it is narrated from Ibn 'Abbas without chain that he said: 'It is between eighteen years and forty.' And apparently, although this is also weak, it is close to the words of the Qur'an because Allah says: 'Until when he reaches the age of strength and reaches forty years.' So it is very possible that Imam Abu Hanifa relied on this weak narration because in this chapter there is no narration stronger than it. Similarly, what Hafiz al-Bayhaqi narrated from Anas: 'When the child completes fifteen years, his wealth and his obligations are written, and the legal punishments are established against him' is also weak, as Hafiz said in al-Talkhis. In any case, adopting the narration of Ibn 'Abbas is precautionary because a person who becomes eighteen years old is considered an adult according to both narrations, unlike one who is fifteen years old, who is considered an adult only according to the narration of Anas and not according to the narration of Ibn 'Abbas. Question: The interpretation of 'ashudd' as twenty, thirty, or forty should be more appropriate than eighteen years. As Hafiz al-Tabarani narrated in al-Mu'jam al-Awsat from Ibn 'Abbas regarding the verse 'until he reaches the age of strength' that he said: 'Thirty-three years, and it is regarding what 'Isa ibn Maryam was raised up.' And in Tafsir Ibn Mardawayh from Ibn 'Abbas: 'until he reaches the age of strength' he said: 'Thirty-nine years.' Answer: Absolutely not, because the dispute between Anas and Ibn 'Abbas is about the beginning of 'ashudd', and the interpretation as twenty etc. gives it an application that Ibn 'Abbas does not deny, for he says: 'It is from eighteen to thirty or forty.' His statement: 'And this is the minimum said about it' etc. That is, regarding the meaning of 'ashudd', the quantities transmitted are different: some mentioned twenty years, some twenty-two, some twenty-five, some thirty-three, some forty, some sixty-two years. Among them, the least quantity is eighteen years, which is the saying of Ibn 'Abbas. So the ruling will be based on it due to certainty. Only this much that the development and puberty of women occur very quickly, so one year was reduced for them because the year consists of four seasons (spring, autumn, summer, winter), one of which will inevitably suit the constitution and nature. His statement: 'For certainty by it...' etc. There is a strong objection to this: Regarding the minor reaching the age of strength, the certain duration is the one that is the greatest among the mentioned durations, not the one that is the least. Because a person who reaches the greatest of them
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a commentary (sharh) on al-Hidayah, discussing the age of puberty (bulugh) in the chapter of interdiction (hajr). The author first addresses the minimum age for menstruation, citing agreement that under five years it is not menstruation, over nine it is, with disagreement for ages 6-8. Some narrate a minimum of 11 years. This part sets the context for the biological onset of puberty.

The core of the passage is the dispute on the age of legal puberty. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam al-Shafi‘i hold that fifteen years is the maximum age for puberty for both males and females, based on widespread custom and the hadith of Ibn ‘Umar who was not accepted for battle at fourteen but was accepted at fifteen. They also cite a hadith from Anas that at fifteen, the child's deeds are recorded and punishments apply.

Imam Abu Hanifa argues that the Quranic verse, “Do not approach the orphan’s property until he reaches the age of strength (ashudd),” indicates a later age. He interprets ashudd as eighteen years for males, based on a narration from Ibn ‘Abbas that it is between eighteen and thirty, taking the minimum to be cautious. For females, he reduces one year to seventeen because they mature earlier, and the year includes seasons that suit the body.

The passage then answers objections: the hadith of Ibn ‘Umar refers to battle capability rather than puberty per se. The added phrase in some narrations, “he considered that I had reached puberty,” is interpreted as physical strength for fighting. The hadith of Anas is declared weak by some critics. The narration from ‘A’ishah that she reached puberty at nine is taken as circumstantial evidence for early female maturity.

The author also discusses the authenticity of the Ibn ‘Abbas narration, noting it is weak but adopted because no stronger evidence exists. The precautionary benefit is that a person of eighteen is considered adult under both views. The passage concludes by addressing an objection about certainty: the minimum is chosen because it is the most cautious, ensuring that anyone reaching that age is definitely adult.

Key Terms
سن بلوغ (sin al-bulugh): The age at which a person reaches legal maturity (adulthood) for fiqh obligations.
اشد (ashudd): The age of strength and full physical/mental maturity, interpreted differently.
حیض (hayd): Menstrual blood that triggers rulings of purity and worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the default age of puberty for a male in the absence of physical signs?
A) 15 years
B) 18 years
C) 17 years
D) 20 years

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, out of precaution, sets the default age of puberty at 18 for males and 17 for females, a view that ensures legal adulthood is not prematurely assigned.

intermediate
8 min
Imam Abu Hanifa's Ruling: No Hajr on a Debtor
States Abu Hanifa's prohibition of hajr on a debtor with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling on hajr for a debtor, explain the dalil from Quran 4:29, and distinguish between hajr and qayd.

Core Idea
Hajr on a debtor destroys legal capacity; imprisonment is the permissible alternative.

This passage from the commentary directly addresses a fundamental difference within the Hanafi school: what should be done with a debtor who refuses to pay? Imam Abu Hanifa takes a strict stance against placing any legal restriction (hajr) on his property, viewing it as a violation of his capacity. Instead, the judge may imprison him. We will examine the reasoning, the Quranic proof, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act being considered is placing legal incapacity (hajr) on a bankrupt debtor. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this act is haram (prohibited).
Hajr here means restricting the debtor's ability to dispose of his property, not imprisonment.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator cites Quran 4:29 as proof. The verse prohibits consuming wealth wrongfully and requires mutual consent in trade.
The dalil is direct from the Quran, making it qat'i al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
If a judge sells the debtor's property without his consent, that is trade without consent, which is covered by the prohibition in the verse. Therefore, hajr (which would enable such sale) is invalid.
The key link is that hajr would allow non-consensual sale, which is explicitly forbidden.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree with Abu Hanifa and allow hajr on a debtor at the creditors' request. This ikhtilaf is acknowledged in the text.
The mufta bihi in later practice is the Sahibayn's view, but this lesson focuses on Abu Hanifa's position.
5
Evaluate the alternative: qayd
Instead of hajr, the judge may imprison (qayd) the debtor to compel him to sell his own property and repay the debt. Imprisonment does not remove legal capacity.
Qayd is coercive but does not affect the debtor's ownership or ability to transact.

قوله لا احجر في الدين ... الخ - اس میں کلمہ کفی سبیہ ہے جیسے کہا جاتا ہے یجب القطع في السرقه امام صاحب فرماتے ہیں کہ مفلس مقروض پر حجر نہیں کیا جا سکتا۔ اگر چہ قرض خواہ لوگ اس کا مطالبہ کریں کیونکہ اس پر حجر کرنا اسکی اہلیت کو بالکلیہ ختم کرنے اور بہائم کے ساتھ ملحق کرنے کے مرادف ہے۔ اسلئے صرف ضرر خاص یعنی ضر ر غرماء کے دفعیہ کی خاطر ایسا نہیں کیا جا سکتا۔ البتہ قاضی اس کو قید کر لے تاکہ وہ ادائیگی قرض کے سلسلہ میں اپنا مال بیچ ڈالے کیونکہ مدیون پر دین کی ادائیگی واجب ہے اور ٹال مٹول ظلم ہے کرلے تو دفع ظلم کے پیش نظر قاضی اس کو قید کر سکتا ہے۔

قوله فان كان له مال .... الخ - پھر اگر مدیون مذکور کا کچھ مال ہو تو حاکم اس میں کچھ تصرف نہیں کرے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی ایک طرح کا حجر ہے۔ نیز اسلئے بھی کہ یہ رضامندی کے بغیر تجارت ہے تو بحکم نص باطل ہو گی۔ چنانچہ حق تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے:
لا تأكلوا اموالكم بينكم بالباطل الا ان تكون تجارة عن تراض منكم
تم لوگ آپس میں اپنے مالوں کو باطل طریقہ پر مت کھاؤ مگر آنکہ تمہاری رضا مندی سے تجارت ہو۔
معلوم ہوا کہ رضامندی کے بغیر جو خرید و فروخت ہو وہ باطل ہے۔ پس جب قاضی نے قرض دار پر اس کی رضامندی کے بغیر اس کا مال فروخت کیا تو بحکم نص باطل ہوگا۔ ہاں قاضی اس قرض دار کو برابر قید رکھے یہاں تک کہ وہ خود اپنے قرضہ میں اس مال کو فروخت کرے تا کہ قرض خواہوں کا حق ادا ہو جائے اور قرض دار کا ظلم دور ہو۔
فائدہ مفلس اور مذکور کو کتنی مدت تک قید میں رکھا جائے؟ اس میں مختلف اقوال ہیں۔ کسی میں دو مہینے ہیں کسی میں تین اور بعض روایات میں چار ماہ سے چھ ماہ تک محبوس رکھنا منقول ہے۔ مگر صحیح یہ ہے کہ اسکی کوئی تحدید نہیں بلکہ یہ مجوس کے حال پر مبنی ہے اس واسطے کہ بعض لوگ معمولی تنبیہ سے گھبرا جاتے ہیں اور بعض لوگ ایسے نڈر ہوتے ہیں کہ عرصہ دراز تک جیل میں رہنے کے باوجود صحیح بات نہیں بتاتے ۔ اسلئے حاکم کی رائے پر محمول ہو گا وہ جتنی مدت تک مناسب سمجھے قید میں رکھے۔ پھر محبوس شرعی یا غیر شرعی کسی ضرورت سے باہر نہیں آ سکتا۔ یہاں تک کہ فقہاء نے تصریح کی ہے کہ ماہ رمضان ، عیدین، جمعه صلوات مکتوبه، حج مفروض اور کسی کے جنازے کی نماز کیلئے بھی باہر نہیں آ سکتا۔ البتہ بعض فقہاء کے نزدیک والدین، اجداد، جدات اور اولاد کے جنازہ کیلئے نکل سکتا ہے۔ بشرطیکہ اپنا کوئی کفیل پیش کر دے فتوی اسی قول پر ہے۔
His statement: 'I do not place a restriction in debt...' etc. In this there is an expression like it is said 'Cutting is obligatory in theft'. Imam Sahib (Abu Hanifa) says: A bankrupt debtor cannot be placed under legal incapacity (hajr). Even if the creditors demand it, because placing hajr on him is akin to completely destroying his capacity and making him like cattle. Therefore, it cannot be done solely for the sake of preventing a specific harm, i.e., the harm to the creditors. However, the judge may imprison him so that he sells his property in the course of paying his debt, because repayment of debt is obligatory on the debtor, and evasion is injustice. So to prevent injustice, the judge can imprison him.

His statement: 'Then if he has property...' etc. Then if the said debtor has some property, the ruler will not dispose of it in any way. Because this is also a type of hajr. Also because it is trade without consent, so by textual ruling it would be invalid. As Allah the Exalted said:
'Do not consume your property among yourselves wrongfully, unless it be trade by mutual consent.'
You should not eat each other's property by false means, except that there be trade with your mutual consent.
Thus it is known that a sale without consent is invalid. So when the judge sold the debtor's property without his consent, it would be invalid by textual ruling. But the judge should keep the debtor imprisoned until he himself sells that property for his debt, so that the creditors' right is fulfilled and the debtor's injustice is removed.

Benefit: For how long should the bankrupt/debtor be imprisoned? There are various opinions. Some say two months, some three, and in some narrations four to six months is reported. But the correct view is that there is no fixed limit; rather it depends on the condition of the [debtor?]. Because some people are deterred by a slight warning, while others are so fearless that they do not speak the truth despite a long stay in prison. Therefore it will be left to the judge's discretion; he may imprison for as long as he deems appropriate. Then the imprisoned person cannot go out for any shar'i or non-shar'i necessity. The jurists have even specified that he cannot go out for Ramadan, the two Eids, Friday, obligatory prayers, obligatory Hajj, or a funeral prayer. However, according to some jurists, he may go out for the funeral of parents, grandparents, and children, provided he provides a guarantor. The fatwa is on this latter opinion.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on legal incapacity (hajr) for a debtor, according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The commentator begins by explaining the matn: Imam Abu Hanifa states that a bankrupt debtor cannot be placed under hajr (legal restriction on disposing of property). Even if creditors demand it, hajr is not allowed. The reason given is that hajr would completely nullify the debtor's legal capacity, reducing him to the status of an animal. Preventing harm to creditors (a specific harm) does not justify such a drastic measure. Instead, the judge may imprison the debtor to compel him to sell his own property and repay debts, since paying debts is obligatory and delaying is injustice.

The second part discusses if the debtor has property: the judge cannot sell it without the debtor's consent because that would also be a form of hajr and would constitute invalid trade. The proof is the Quranic verse (4:29) which prohibits consuming wealth wrongfully and requires mutual consent in trade. Sales without consent are void. So the judge cannot sell; he can only imprison until the debtor sells himself.

The fā'idah (benefit) addresses the duration of imprisonment: there is no fixed period. It depends on the debtor's character. Some are deterred quickly, others are obstinate. The judge uses his discretion. The passage then lists that the imprisoned debtor cannot leave for even religious duties like Ramadan, Eid, Friday prayer, Hajj, or funerals, except that some jurists allow leaving for funerals of close relatives (parents, grandparents, children) if a guarantor is provided. The fatwa is on this exception.

This is a clear ruling from the Hanafi school, based on textual proof (Quran) and rational consideration (preventing greater harm by restricting freedom rather than property).

Key Terms
حجر (hajr): Legal restriction placed on a person's capacity to dispose of property, making them like a minor or a fool.
مفلس (mufallis): A bankrupt debtor whose debts exceed his assets, and he has been declared insolvent by the judge.
قید (qayd): Imprisonment by the judge to compel the debtor to sell his property and repay debts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what can the judge do if a debtor refuses to pay his debt?
A) Place a legal restriction (hajr) on the debtor
B) Imprison the debtor until he sells his property
C) Sell the debtor's property without his consent
D) Declare the debtor bankrupt and distribute his property

Key Takeaway
Hajr on a debtor is prohibited by Abu Hanifa; the judge may imprison to coerce payment without destroying legal capacity.

Sahibayn's View: Hajr Permitted at Creditors' Request
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hajr for debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Sahibayn's position on hajr for debt and evaluate the Hanafi response to the opposing proof from tilji'ah.

Core Idea
Fatwa is on the Sahibayn’s view that a debtor can be placed under legal incapacity (hajr) to prevent fraudulent sales.

This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding placing legal incapacity (hajr) on a bankrupt debtor at the request of creditors. While Imam Abu Hanifa held that hajr destroys legal capacity and is impermissible, his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), permitted it to protect creditors from fraudulent conveyances (tilji'ah). The later Hanafi tradition adopted the Sahibayn's view as the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding hajr for debt. Note that Abu Hanifa prohibits it; the Sahibayn permit it with conditions.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; both views derive from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
Examine the qiyas (analogy) on safīh (spendthrift): hajr is allowed for the safīh's benefit, and here it is for the creditors' benefit. Also consider the concern of tilji'ah (fraudulent sale).
The proof is aqli (rational) based on prevention of harm.
3
Identify the opposing proof
Understand Abu Hanifa's counterargument: hajr destroys legal capacity and is harmful to the debtor; the analogy to safīh is flawed because safīh's hajr benefits him, while debtor's hajr benefits others. Also, tilji'ah is speculative.
Abu Hanifa prefers imprisonment over hajr.
4
Follow the meta-discussion
Note the debate on whether hajr due to debt depends on a prior verdict of bankruptcy (qada bil-iflas). Some shaykhs say it does; others say it is independent. The text argues independence because the ruling applies even when property is manifest (contradicting bankruptcy).
This shows the depth of Hanafi usul in refining the scope of a ruling.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Multiple late Hanafi works (Durr Mukhtar, Bazzaziyya, etc.) confirm that fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view. Identify the tarjih authority and the practical implication.
The mufta bihi is that hajr can be imposed, but only sales below market price are prohibited.

قوله و قالا اذا طلب ..... الخ - صاحبین اور ائمہ ثلاثہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر قرض خواہ لوگ مقروض مفلس پر حجر قائم کرنے کی درخواست کریں تو اس پر حجر کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ پس قاضی اس کو فروختگی اور ہر طرح کے تصرف اور اقر را کرنے سے منع کر دے گا۔ تا کہ قرض خواہوں کا نقصان نہ ہو ۔ بدلیل آنکہ سفیہ پر جو حجر کو جائز رکھا گیا ہے وہ اس کے حق میں بہتری کے پیش نظر رکھا گیا ہے اور مفلس پر حجر کرنے میں غرماء کی بہتری ہے۔ کیونکہ ہو سکتا ہے۔ مفلس مذکور اپنا مال تلجیہ کے طور پر فروخت کر دے۔ تو قرض خواہوں کا حق مٹ جائے گا۔ پھر صاحبین کے قول و تمنعه من البيع كا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ثمن مثل سے کم کے عوض فروخت کرنے سے منع کرے گا۔ اگر وہ شمن مثل کے عوض فروخت کرے تو اس سے منع نہیں کرے گا۔ کیونکہ اس سے غرماء کا حق فوت نہیں ہوتا۔ اختیار، درمختار، تنویر صحیح قدوری ، بزازیہ، جو ہرہ ، قاضی خان ملتقی اور طائی شرح کنز وغیرہ میں ہے کہ نفس حجر میں اور مدیون کا اسباب و جائداد فروخت کرنے میں فتویٰ صاحبین کے قول پر ہے۔
فائدہ میجی بتشدید نیم لما تجویز سے ہے بمعنی ورثاء کیلئے خاص کر دینا اور فقہاء کے یہاں تجلیہ اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ کسی ایسے فعل کے کرنے پر مجبور کرے جس کا ظاہر باطن کے خلاف ہو ۔ یہاں اس سے مراد یہ ہے کہ مفلس اپنا مال کسی ایسے بڑے آدمی کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دے جس کے قبضہ سے نکالنا ممکن نہ ہو۔
قوله غرماء المفلس ... الخ - اس پر یہ اعتراض ہوتا ہے کہ مجور علیہ کا مفلس ہونا ضروری نہیں ۔ بلکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک حق غرماء کی خاطر غنی پر بھی حجر کرنا جائز ہے۔ بلکہ دین کے سبب سے جبر کرنا تو صحیح معنی میں غنی ہی کے حق میں سود مند ہوتا ہے نہ کہ مفلس کے حق میں، پیس مسئلہ کی وضع میں لفظ مفلس کا ذکر خلل انداز ہے۔ سوال نہایہ وغیرہ میں ذخیرہ سے منقول ہے کہ ہمارے بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ دین کے سبب سے حجر کرنے کا مسئلہ قضاء بالا فلاس پر مبنی ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر مدیون پر حکم افلاس ہوئے بغیر ابتداء حجر کیا گیا تو اس کا حجر بلا خلاف صحیح نہ ہوگا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک بحالت حیات افلاس کا تحقق ہو جاتا ہے۔ تو قاضی کے افلاس کا حکم کرنا اور اس پر مبنی کر کے حجر کرنا ممکن ہے اور امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک زندگی کی حالت میں افلاس متحقق نہیں ہوتا تو قاضی کیلئے اولاً افلاس کا حکم کرنا اور اس پر مبنی کر کے حجر کرنا ناممکن ہے۔ اور بعض مشائخ نے مسئلہ حجر بسبب الدین کو مستقل مسئلہ قرار دیا ہے۔ مسئلہ قضاء بالافلاس پر مبنی نہیں مانا۔ اس قول پر امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک حجر سے جو امر مانع ہے وہ حجر کا مجور کے حق میں الحاق ضرر کو تضمن ہونا ہے جس کا قضاء بالافلاس سے کوئی تعلق نہیں ہے۔ اھ پس ممکن ہے کہ مسئلہ کتاب کی وضع میں مفلس کا ذکر ان لوگوں کا قول اختیار کرنے پر ہو جنہوں نے اس مسئلہ حج کو مسئلہ قضاء بالافلاس پر مبنی مانا ہے۔ جواب صاحب کتاب کا مذہب ابوحنیفہ کے بیان میں یہ کہنا وان کان لہ مال لم يتصرف فیہ الحاکم او رمذہب صاحبین کی دلیل کے بیان میں یہ کہنا لانه عساه يلجى ما له اسی طرح یہ کہنا وباع ماله ان امتنع المفلس من بيعہ یہ سب اسی پر دال ہے کہ مسئلہ کا ماله مدار قول مذکور کے اختیار کرنے پر نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ ظہور مال کی صورت میں قضاء بالافلاس کا تصور ہی نہیں ہوسکتا حالانکہ کتاب کے مذکورہ اقوال میں ظہور مال کی تصریح موجود ہے ) بلکہ مسئلہ کا مدار اس کے مستقل ہونے پر ہے۔
مفلس مال کی بیج سے باز رہے تو قاضی بیع کرے اور قرض خواہوں میں حصہ دین تقسیم کر دے
قال وباع ماله ان امتنع المفلس من بيعه وقسمه بين غرمائه بالحصص عندهما لان البيع مستحق عليه لايفاء دينه حتى يُحبس لاجله فاذا امتنع ناب القاضی منابه كما فى الجب والعنة قلنا التلجية موهومة والمستحق قضاء الدين والبيع ليس بطريق متعين لذلك بخلاف الجب والعنة والحبس لقضاء الدين بما يختاره من الطريق كيف وان صح البيع كان الحبس اضرارا بهما بتاخير حق الدائن وتعذيب المديون فلا يكون مشروعا ترجمہ اور قاضی فروخت کرے اس کا مال اگر مفلس اس کی بیع سے باز رہے اور اس کے قرض خواہوں کے درمیان حصہ رسد تقسیم کر دے صاحبین کے نزدیک ۔ کیونکہ فروخت کرنا اس پر واجب ہے اپنا قرض چکانے کیلئے یہاں تک کہ وہ اس کی وجہ سے قید کیا جاتا ہے۔ ہیں
His statement: 'And they said: When they demand...' etc. – The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and the three Imams say: If the creditors request to establish restriction (hajr) on the bankrupt debtor, then hajr can be imposed. So the judge will prohibit him from selling and from all types of transactions and acknowledgments, so that the creditors do not suffer loss. The proof is that hajr placed on a spendthrift (safīh) is for his own benefit, while hajr on a bankrupt is for the benefit of the creditors. Because it is possible that the said bankrupt may sell his property as tilji'ah (fraudulent conveyance), thereby eliminating the creditors' right. Then the meaning of the Sahibayn's statement 'and he prevents him from selling' is that he will prevent him from selling for less than the fair market price (thaman mithl). If he sells for the fair market price, he will not prevent him, because that does not cause loss to the creditors. In al-Ikhtiyar, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, Tanwir, Sahih al-Quduri, al-Bazzaziyya, al-Jawhara, Qadi Khan, Multaqa, and the Ta'i commentary of al-Kanz, it is stated that the fatwa is on the statement of the Sahibayn regarding the hajr itself and selling the debtor's assets.

Benefit: 'Mejee' with tashdid... 'tilji'ah' is from the root meaning to set aside specifically for heirs. Among the jurists, tilji'ah is defined as compelling someone to do an act whose outward appearance contradicts the inner intention. Here it means that a bankrupt sells his property to some influential person from whose possession it cannot be taken out.

His statement: 'The creditors of the bankrupt...' etc. – An objection arises: the person subject to hajr does not necessarily have to be bankrupt. Rather, according to the Sahibayn, hajr can be placed on a wealthy person for the sake of creditors. In fact, compulsion due to debt is more beneficial for a wealthy person than for a bankrupt. Thus the mention of 'bankrupt' in the formulation of the issue is problematic. A question is quoted from al-Zakhira in al-Nihayah that some of our shaykhs said: The issue of hajr due to debt is based on the verdict of bankruptcy (qadā bil-iflās). So if hajr is initiated without a verdict of bankruptcy, it is invalid without dispute. According to the Sahibayn, bankruptcy is realized during the life of the debtor, so it is possible for the judge to pronounce bankruptcy and then base hajr on it. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, bankruptcy is not realized during life, so the judge cannot first pronounce bankruptcy and then base hajr on it. And some shaykhs considered the issue of hajr due to debt as an independent issue, not based on the verdict of bankruptcy. According to this, the obstacle to hajr for Imam Abu Hanifa is that hajr entails harm to the person subject to it, which has no connection with the verdict of bankruptcy. So it is possible that the mention of 'bankrupt' in the book is following the opinion of those who consider this issue to be based on the verdict of bankruptcy. The answer: The author's expression in describing the madhhab of Abu Hanifa as 'if he has property, the ruler does not dispose of it' and in describing the proof of the Sahibayn as 'because perhaps he will practice tilji'ah with his property', and similarly his statement 'and he sells his property if the bankrupt refrains from selling it' – all this indicates that the issue is not based on adopting the aforementioned opinion, because in the presence of manifest property, the concept of a verdict of bankruptcy is impossible, while the book's statements explicitly mention manifest property. Rather, the issue is based on its independence.

'If the bankrupt refrains from selling his property, the judge sells it and distributes the shares among his creditors.' He said: 'And he sells his property if the bankrupt refrains from selling it, and distributes it among his creditors according to shares, according to the two (Sahibayn). Because selling is obligatory on him to fulfill his debt, even to the extent that he is imprisoned for it. So if he refrains, the judge stands in his place, as in the case of impotence (jabb) and being a eunuch ('unnah). We say: The fear of tilji'ah is speculative, and what is required is the payment of the debt, and selling is not the only prescribed method for that, unlike the cases of jabb and 'unnah. Moreover, if selling is valid, then imprisonment would be harmful to both parties – delaying the creditor's right and torturing the debtor – so it would not be prescribed.' Translation: And the judge sells his property if the bankrupt refrains from selling it, and distributes among his creditors according to shares, according to the Sahibayn. Because selling is obligatory on him to pay off his debt, to the extent that he is imprisoned for it. They are.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This extensive passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute concerning hajr (legal incapacity) on a debtor. It begins by stating the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) along with the three Imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad): if creditors request, the judge can place hajr on the bankrupt debtor, prohibiting him from all transactions and acknowledgments to prevent harm. Their proof is analogical (qiyas): just as hajr is allowed for a spendthrift (safīh) for his own benefit, here it is for the benefit of creditors, as the debtor might sell his property fraudulently (tilji'ah) to evade payment.

The commentary then clarifies that the prohibition to sell is only for sales below market price; sales at market price are not prohibited because they don't harm creditors. It then cites multiple Hanafi works stating that the fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view.

A benefit (fā'idah) defines tilji'ah: originating from the root 'to set aside', it means compelling someone to an act where the external form contradicts the inner intention. Here it refers to the debtor selling to a powerful person from whom the property cannot be recovered.

Next, an objection is raised: the mention of 'bankrupt' in the issue is problematic because according to Sahibayn, hajr can be on a wealthy person too. This leads into a discussion about whether hajr due to debt depends on a prior verdict of bankruptcy (qadā bil-iflās). Some shaykhs say it does; others say it is independent. The author argues that the expressions in the book (al-Hidayah) itself indicate independence, because they mention manifest property while bankruptcy verdict is impossible with manifest property (since bankruptcy implies no visible property). Therefore the ruling is independent.

Finally, the text presents the Arabic matn: if the bankrupt refrains from selling, the judge sells and distributes. This is the Sahibayn's position. The proof is that sale is obligatory on the debtor to repay debt, so the judge acts in his stead when he refuses, analogous to cases of impotence (jabb) and being a eunuch ('unnah) where the judge can annul marriage. A rebuttal is given: the analogy is weak because tilji'ah is speculative, and the primary obligation is payment of debt, not necessarily sale. Moreover, if the judge sells, then imprisonment becomes harmful to both parties, so it would not be prescribed. This rebuttal likely reflects Abu Hanifa's position or a later refinement.

The passage ends with a brief translation repeating the ruling.

Overall, this lesson illuminates the complexities of Hanafi jurisprudence: the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his students, the underlying rational proofs, and the meta-discussion about whether the ruling is procedural (based on bankruptcy verdict) or substantive.

Key Terms
تلجیہ (tilji'ah): A fraudulent sale where the debtor sells to a powerful person to place the property beyond the reach of creditors; the outward form is a sale but the inner intention is to defeat creditors' rights.
غرماء (ghuramā'): Creditors who are owed debts by the bankrupt debtor.
قضاء بالافلاس (qadā' bil-iflās): A judge's verdict that a debtor is bankrupt (iflas), which triggers certain legal consequences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, when can a judge prevent a debtor from selling his property?
A) The judge can prevent any sale, regardless of price, because the debtor is under hajr.
B) The judge can only prevent sales below the fair market price (thaman mithl).
C) The judge cannot prevent any sale; only imprisonment is allowed.
D) The judge can prevent sales only if the debtor is wealthy, not if he is bankrupt.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that a judge may place hajr on a debtor to prevent below-market sales, based on the Sahibayn's view, despite Imam Abu Hanifa's prohibition.

Acknowledgment (Iqrar) by a Person Under Interdiction
Ruling with proof on acknowledgment by a debtor under interdiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an acknowledgment made by a debtor under interdiction and explain the distinction between existing and newly acquired property.

Core Idea
A debtor's acknowledgment during interdiction is suspended; it binds after debts are paid, but immediately valid for new property.

When a debtor is under interdiction (hajr) due to unpaid debts, his ability to make binding acknowledgments (iqrar) is restricted. This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies the rule: an acknowledgment does not take effect immediately against property that is already subject to creditors' rights. However, if the debtor acquires new property after interdiction, his acknowledgment in that new property is effective straightaway. The reasoning draws a sharp contrast between a mere statement (iqrar) and an overt act like destruction (istihlak).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Who performs it and under what condition? The act is an acknowledgment (iqrar) by a debtor who is under interdiction (hajr). The ruling: it is not immediately binding; it becomes binding only after prior debts are paid.
The rule applies to existing property at the time of interdiction.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is rational (dalil aqli): the property already has the right of earlier creditors attached to it, so the debtor cannot nullify their right by acknowledging for someone else. This is contrasted with destruction (istihlak), which is an observable act that cannot be reversed.
The proof is logical, not scriptural.
3
Distinguish existing vs. new property
If the debtor acquires property after interdiction, his acknowledgment in that new property is immediately effective because the prior creditors' right does not attach to it (it did not exist at the time of interdiction).
This is an exception to the general rule.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi attribution
The commentary mentions that this ruling is according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Abu Hanifa's view is not explicitly stated here, but the text implies agreement.
The authority is Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
Map the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i has two opinions: if the acknowledged debt existed before interdiction, the acknowledgment is valid and binding (in the soundest view); another view says it is not binding. The Hanafi rebuttal is that creditors' rights take precedence.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with practical consequences.

Source Text

Whether a debtor under interdiction made an acknowledgment, it will be binding or not. He said: If he acknowledges during the state of interdiction with an acknowledgment, it becomes binding upon him after the payment of debts, because the right of the first (creditors) is attached to this property, so he cannot nullify their right by acknowledging for others. Contrary to destruction, because it is witnessed and cannot be repelled. And if he acquires other property after interdiction, his acknowledgment is effective therein, because their right is not attached to it due to its non-existence at the time of interdiction. Translation: If the debtor made an acknowledgment during the state of interdiction, it will be binding upon him after paying the debts, because the right of the earlier (creditors) is attached to this property, so he cannot nullify their right by acknowledging for others. Unlike destroying, because that is witnessed and cannot be repelled. And if he acquires some other property after interdiction, his acknowledgment therein is effective, because their right is not attached to it due to its non-existence at the time of interdiction. Commentary on 'if he acknowledges...': Then if the aforementioned debtor made an acknowledgment during the state of interdiction, that acknowledgment will not be immediately binding, but will be binding after paying the debts. Because the right of the previous creditors is already attached to this existing property, so he cannot nullify their right by acknowledging for others. Commentary
This passage discusses the validity of an acknowledgment (iqrar) made by a debtor who is under interdiction (hajr). The ruling from the matn is that such an acknowledgment, if made during interdiction, is not immediately binding. It becomes binding only after the existing debts have been paid. The reason is that the property already has a right attached to it from the earlier creditors; the debtor cannot use an acknowledgment to defraud them. This is different from destroying the property (istihlak), which is an observable act that cannot be reversed. If the debtor acquires new property after the interdiction, his acknowledgment regarding that new property is valid immediately because the creditors' right does not attach to it since it was not in existence at the time of interdiction. The commentary explains that this is according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). It also notes the view of Imam al-Shafi'i: if the acknowledgment is for a debt that was incurred before the interdiction, it is valid and binding in the soundest opinion; another opinion says it is not binding. The text cuts off after mentioning Imam Malik.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a right or debt against oneself; a legal admission.
حجر (hajr): Interdiction, legal restriction on a person's capacity to manage property due to debt or other reasons.
استهلاک (istihlak): Destruction or consumption of property, which is an observable act that cannot be undone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only if the qadi approves
D) No, it is suspended until all prior debts are paid

Key Takeaway
An acknowledgment by a debtor under interdiction is suspended for assets existing at interdiction but immediately effective for assets acquired afterward.

Selling Currency vs Goods for Debt: Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Order of Sale
Intra-Hanafi dispute on selling currency for debt and the subsequent order of asset sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding selling a debtor's currency without permission and apply the mufta bihi order of asset sale for debt repayment.

Core Idea
Currency is a means, not an end — its forced sale for debt is disputed; the Sahibayn's view is mufta bihi, requiring cash sold first when debt is in cash.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement about selling a debtor's currency (nuqud) to repay a debt without his permission. Imam Abu Hanifa considers it impermissible by istihsan, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) permit it by qiyas. The commentary clarifies the difference between currency and goods, and then provides the practical order of selling assets based on the Sahibayn's view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling and the Sahibayn's ruling on selling currency without permission.
Abu Hanifa: not permissible without permission (istihsan). Sahibayn: permissible by qiyas.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The opponent here is the Sahibayn within the Hanafi school. They hold that selling currency is permissible by qiyas, analogizing it to selling any other property.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Sahibayn's qiyas: currency is owned property like goods, so it can be sold to repay debts. The passage does not detail the illa but implies it is the property status.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa uses istihsan to override the qiyas, arguing that currency is a medium, not an end, and its forced sale resembles riba. The commentary notes that the ruling is specific to Abu Hanifa.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa, the judge cannot sell cash without the debtor's permission; under the Sahibayn, he can. The mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn's view, and the passage then gives the order of sale based on that view.
Order: if debt is in dirhams, sell cash first, then goods, then property, starting with the easiest.

That is, when according to the Sahibayn, selling the debtor's property becomes permissible, then for the debtor's debt, first currencies will be sold, when the debt is in dirhams and the debtor's property is also cash dirhams. Because in this there is haste in paying the debt and also consideration for the debtor. And from the debtor's clothing, one set will be left and the rest sold. Because one set is sufficient for clothing. According to some scholars, two sets will be left, because when he washes clothes, it is necessary to have something to wear.

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of a bankrupt's assets for debt repayment. The passage first clarifies that Imam Abu Hanifa does not permit the sale of currency (naqd) without permission because it is a sale of currency (sarf), which is subject to strict rules. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) permit it by qiyas, considering it a valid sale. The commentator cites Sahib Nata'ij to justify Abu Hanifa's view, arguing that the ruling is specific to him. Then the commentary explains the difference between currency and goods: goods have intrinsic benefit, while currency is merely a medium. Based on the Sahibayn's view, the order of selling assets is given: first cash (if the debt is in cash), then goods, then property, starting with the easiest. The debtor is allowed to keep one set of clothing (two according to some scholars) to maintain his dignity.

عروض (urud): Goods; commodities other than cash, such as merchandise.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of departing from qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling.

Acknowledgment by a Bankrupt During Interdiction: Inter-Madhhab Analysis
Ruling on acknowledgment by bankrupt during interdiction with inter-madhhab differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the validity and binding nature of acknowledgment by a bankrupt during interdiction, and apply the exception for property destruction.

Core Idea
A bankrupt's acknowledgment is valid but deferred to protect prior creditors; destruction triggers immediate liability.

This passage from the Book of Hajr (Interdiction) addresses a critical tension: when a bankrupt person acknowledges a new debt during interdiction, does that acknowledgment immediately bind him and affect his creditors? The Hanafi school, according to the Sahibayn, holds that such acknowledgment is valid but its effect is postponed until all prior debts are paid. The Shafi'i school, along with Malik and Ahmad, holds that if the acknowledged debt existed before interdiction, it is binding immediately. The exception of property destruction (istihlak) is also discussed: unlike mere words, a physical act of destruction creates instant liability. In this lesson, we will dissect the legal reasoning behind each position and understand the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: the bankrupt's acknowledgment during interdiction is valid but binding only after all prior debts are paid. Note the authority: this is the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) as recorded in the Zahir al-Riwayah.
The position is not that the acknowledgment is invalid, but that it is deferred.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that if the acknowledged debt existed before interdiction, the acknowledgment is valid and binding immediately. This is also the view of Malik and Ahmad. Note that there is a weaker Shafi'i opinion that it is not binding.
The dispute hinges on whether the right of prior creditors overrides the acknowledgment.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i position rests on the idea that acknowledgment is a form of testimony (shahada) and that the debt, if pre-existing, is a true obligation that should be honoured. The property is merely the means of satisfaction, not the subject of the right.
The Hanafi response challenges this by focusing on the attachment of creditors' rights to the property.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi argument is that the right of prior creditors has attached to the existing property (ta'alluq al-haqq). Thus, the bankrupt cannot prejudice that right by acknowledging for others. Interdiction (hajr) restricts his capacity to act in a way that harms creditors. The exception of destruction (istihlak) is physical and irrevocable, so it bypasses the restriction.
The distinction between mere words and physical acts is key: 'interdiction does not apply to a physical act'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In Hanafi law, the new creditor (by acknowledgment) must wait until all prior debts are paid. In Shafi'i law, the new creditor is treated equally and can claim immediately if the debt predates interdiction. This affects the distribution of assets in bankruptcy.
The Hanafi position protects prior creditors more strongly, while Shafi'i treats acknowledgment as a valid proof of debt regardless of timing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ: اگر مدیون نے حالت حجر میں کوئی اقرار کیا تو یہ لازم ہو گا اس کو ادائیگی دیون کے بعد کیونکہ اس مال کے ساتھ پہلوں کا حق وابستہ ہو چکا تو وہ ان کے غیر کیلئے اقرار کرنے سے ان کا حق باطل نہیں کر سکتا۔ بخلاف ہلاک کر دینے کے۔ کیونکہ یہ تو آنکھوں سے مشاہدہ ہے جس کا کچھ دفعیہ نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اور اگر اس نے حجر کے بعد کچھ اور مال حاصل کیا تو اس میں اس کا اقرار نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس مال سے ان کا حق وابستہ نہیں ہوا بوقت حجر اس مال کے موجود نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے۔

تشریح: قوله فان اقر ... الخ - پھر اگر مدیون مذکور نے حجر کی حالت میں کوئی اقرار کیا تو وہ اقرار بالفعل لازم نہ ہوگا بلکہ ادائیگی دیون کے بعد لازم ہوگا۔ شرح اقطع میں ہے کہ یہ صاحبین کے قول پر ہے۔ کیونکہ اس مال موجود کے ساتھ پہلے قرض خواہوں کا حق وابستہ ہو چکا ہے تو وہ ان کے علاوہ کیلئے اقرار کر کے ان کے حق کو باطل نہیں کر سکتا۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک اگر مدیون نے ایسے دین کا اقرار کیا جو اس کے ذمہ حجر سے پہلے لازم ہوا تھا تو اقرار صحیح ہوگا اور اصح قول میں اس پر لازم ہوگا اور ایک قول یہ بھی ہے کہ لازم نہ ہوگا۔ امام مالک اور امام احمد کا قول بھی یہی ہے۔

كتاب الحجر
امام احمد کا قول بھی یہی ہے۔

قوله بخلاف الاستهلاك...... الخ - قول سابق لزمه ذلك بعد قضاء الدیون سے متعلق ہے۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر مدیون نے بحالت حجر کسی کا مال تلف کر دیا تو اس کا تاوان بالفعل لازم ہوگا اور جس کا مال تلف کیا ہے وہ دیگر قرض خواہوں کے ساتھ شریک ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اختلاف تو مشاہد اور محسوس اور آنکھوں سے دیکھی بات ہے جس کا کوئی دفعیہ نہیں ہو سکتا۔ لان الحجر لا يصح في الفعل الحسى
If he acknowledges during the state of interdiction with an acknowledgment, that will be binding upon him after the payment of debts, because the right of the earlier (creditors) has attached to this property, so he cannot invalidate their right by acknowledging for others. Unlike destruction, because it is witnessed and cannot be repelled. And if he acquires other property after interdiction, his acknowledgment in it is effective, because their right did not attach to it due to its non-existence at the time of interdiction.

Translation: If the debtor made an acknowledgment during interdiction, it will be binding upon him after payment of debts, because the right of the earlier ones has attached to this property, so he cannot invalidate their right by acknowledging for others. Unlike destroying (property), because this is witnessed and cannot be repelled. And if he acquired some other property after interdiction, his acknowledgment in it is effective, because their right did not attach to it due to its non-existence at the time of interdiction.

Commentary: His saying: 'if he acknowledges...' etc. Then if the aforementioned debtor made an acknowledgment in the state of interdiction, that acknowledgment will not be immediately binding, but will be binding after payment of debts. In Sharh Aqta' it is that this is according to the Sahibayn. Because with this existing property, the right of the earlier creditors has already attached, so he cannot invalidate their right by acknowledging for others. According to Imam Shafi'i, if the debtor acknowledged a debt that became obligatory upon him before interdiction, the acknowledgment is valid and in the more correct view it is binding upon him, and there is also a view that it is not binding. Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad hold the same view.

His saying: 'unlike destruction...' etc. This relates to the previous statement 'it will be binding after payment of debts'. The meaning is that if the debtor during interdiction destroyed someone's property, his compensation is immediately binding, and the one whose property was destroyed will share with the other creditors. Because destruction is witnessed and perceived, seen with the eyes, and cannot be repelled. Because interdiction does not apply to a physical act.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage addresses the validity of an acknowledgment (iqrar) made by a bankrupt person while under judicial interdiction (hajr). The Hanafi position, according to the Sahibayn, is that such an acknowledgment is not binding immediately but becomes binding after all prior debts are paid. This is because the existing property is already encumbered by the creditors' rights. An exception is made for destroying property (istihlak): if the bankrupt destroys someone's property, the liability is immediate because it is a physical act that cannot be reversed. If the bankrupt acquires new property after interdiction, his acknowledgment regarding that property is effective because the creditors' rights had not attached to it. The passage also notes the Shafi'i view: if the acknowledged debt existed before interdiction, the acknowledgment is valid and binding in the more correct opinion, whereas Malik and Ahmad agree with it being binding.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment; a declaration by a person that he owes a debt or is liable to another.
حجر (hajr): Interdiction; a legal restriction on a person's capacity to manage property, imposed due to bankruptcy or incapacity.
استهلاك (istihlak): Destruction; causing the loss of someone's property by one's action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on an acknowledgment made by a bankrupt during interdiction regarding a debt that was incurred before the interdiction order?
A) The acknowledgment is invalid because interdiction suspends legal capacity.
B) The acknowledgment is valid and immediately binding.
C) The acknowledgment is valid but its effect is deferred until prior debts are paid.
D) The acknowledgment is binding only if it is attested by witnesses.

Key Takeaway
A bankrupt's acknowledgment during interdiction is valid but deferred to protect prior creditors; destruction of property creates immediate liability because it is a physical act.
