تشريح ... قوله ولا يباع ثانياً .... الخ - غلام مذکور کے شمن سے اگر دیون کی پوری ادا ئیگی نہ ہو تو اس کو دوبارہ فروخت نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ تاکہ پہلی بی منع نہ ہو جائے۔ یعنی مشتری کو جب اس بات کا علم ہو گا کہ جو غلام اس نے خریدا ہے وہ اس کی اجازت کے بغیر دوباره فروخت کر دیا جائے گا تو وہ اس خرید سے باز رہے گا یا وہ دوبارہ اسلئے نہیں بیچا جائے گا تا کہ مشتری سے ضرر دور ہو۔ اسلئے کہ مشتری نے تو اس کو تجارت کی اجازت نہیں دی تو وہ اس کے دین کے سبب سے اس کی بیع پر راضی نہیں اب اگر اس کے باوجود اس کو فروخت کیا جائے تو مشتری پر اس کے التزام کے بغیر ضر ر لازم آئے گا۔ بخلاف آقا کے کہ اس نے غلام کو تجارت کی اجازت دے کر اس ضرر کا التزام کیا ہے۔ قوله و يتعلق به دينه ..... الخ عبد مازون کے قرضے اس کی کمائی سے متعلق ہوں گے ۔ خواہ یہ کمائی حقوق دین سے پہلے حاصل ہوئی ہو یا اس کے بعد ۔ نیز جو ہبہ وہ قبول کرے اس سے بھی متعلق ہوں گے۔ اسلئے کہ موہوب کی ملکیت میں آقا جو اس کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے وہ اس وقت ہوتا ہے جب وہ کمائی غلام کی ضرورت سے فارغ ہو۔ حالانکہ وہ ابھی اسی کی ضرورت سے فارغ نہیں ہوئی کیونکہ ہنوز قرضہ اس سے متعلق ہے تو آقا ابھی اس کا خلیفہ نہیں ہو سکتا۔ حاصل یہ کہ ہر وہ کمائی یا ہبہ جو ہنوز غلام کے قبضہ میں ہے اور اس کی ضرورت سے فارغ نہ ہو اس سے دین متعلق ہوگا۔ البتہ ایسے مال سے قرضہ متعلق نہ ہو گا جو حوق دین سے پہلے آقا نے غلام کے قبضہ سے نکال لیا ہو۔ کیونکہ اس میں آقا کیلئے خالص ملکیت ہو جانے کی شرط پائی گئی کہ وہ اس کے غلام کی کمائی ہے جس سے کسی قرض خواہ کا حق متعلق نہیں ہے۔ قوله وله ان ياخذ الخ - غلام پر لحوق دین کے بعد آقا کو اختیار ہے کہ ایسے غلام کا جو محاصل ہو وہ لے لے ۔ کیونکہ آقا کو اگر یہ قدرت نہ دی جائے تو وہ مجبور کر دے گا اور کمائی حاصل ہی نہ ہوگی۔ پھر اس کے مثل محاصل سے جو زائد ہو وہ قرض خواہوں کو واپس دے دے کیونکہ زائدہ کے حق میں کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور غرماء کا حق مقدم ہے۔
Commentary ... His statement: 'And he will not be sold a second time' etc. - If the debts are not fully paid from the price of the mentioned slave, he will not be sold a second time, so that the first sale is not prevented. That is, when the buyer knows that the slave he bought will be sold again without his permission, he will refrain from this purchase. Or he will not be sold again to remove harm from the buyer. Because the buyer did not give him permission for trade, so he is not satisfied with his sale due to his debt. Now if despite that he is sold, harm would befall the buyer without his undertaking. Contrary to the master, who undertook this harm by giving the slave permission for trade. His statement: 'And his debt attaches to it' etc. - The debts of the ma'dhun slave attach to his earnings, whether this earning was acquired before the rights of debt or after. Also, whatever gift he accepts attaches to it. Because the master, who stands in his place regarding ownership of the gifted property, does so when that earning is free from the slave's need. But it is not yet free from his need because the debt still attaches to it, so the master cannot be his successor. The conclusion is that every earning or gift that is still in the slave's possession and not free from his need, the debt attaches to it. However, the debt does not attach to that property which the master removed from the slave's hand before the debt occurred, because the condition of its being pure ownership for the master is found, as it is the earnings of his slave with which no creditor's right is attached. His statement: 'And he may take' etc. - After the debt attaches to the slave, the master has the option to take the profit of such a slave. Because if this power is not given to the master, he will restrict him and no earning will be obtained. Then whatever is excess over the equivalent profit, he returns to the creditors, because there is no need for the excess and the creditors' right is prior.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This section of the commentary provides detailed reasoning for three points in the matn. First, the slave is not sold a second time if the first sale's price doesn't cover all debts, to prevent deterring buyers and to avoid harm to the purchaser who did not consent to the trade debts (as opposed to the master who gave permission for trade). Second, the slave's debts attach to his earnings and any gifts he accepts, because the master only replaces the slave in ownership after the slave's needs are satisfied—which hasn't happened yet due to the debt. However, debts do not attach to property the master removed before the debt. Third, after the debt is incurred, the master may take an amount equivalent to the normal profit (ghullat) of such a slave, because otherwise he would restrict the slave and no earnings would be made. Any excess over the normal profit must be returned to the creditors since their right is prior.

Key Terms
محاصل (mahasal): profit or income of the slave
غلة مثل (ghullat mithl): the equivalent profit or income of a similar slave
عبد مأذون (abd ma'dhun): a slave permitted by his master to engage in trade

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the commentary, why does the debt not attach to property the master removed from the slave before the debt occurred?
A) Because the master is the owner of all slave property.
B) Because the condition of pure ownership for the master is found, as no creditor's right was attached.
C) Because the slave consented to the master's removal.
D) Because the property was already spent.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school balances the master's property rights and creditors' claims by limiting the master's take to the normal profit and securing debt attachment to remaining earnings.

The Condition of Public Knowledge for the Master's Restriction on the Ma'dhun Slave
Ruling on when the master's restriction takes effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that makes the master's restriction (hajr) on the ma'dhun slave effective and apply it to scenarios involving public knowledge.

Core Idea
The master's restriction requires public knowledge to protect innocent third parties.

In this lesson, we examine the precise condition for the validity of the master's restriction (hajr) on a ma'dhun slave. The Hanafi school establishes that the restriction does not take effect until it becomes notorious among the market people. This protects those who deal with the slave based on his apparent permission. The text from Al-Hidayah details the requirement of shuyu' (notoriety) and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act under discussion
The master's act of restricting (placing hajr) on a ma'dhun slave who had been given permission to trade.
The restriction aims to revoke the slave's trading authority.
2
State the condition for effectiveness
The restriction is not effective until it becomes public knowledge (shuyu') among the people of the market (a'immah al-suq). It must be known to most of them.
Merely informing the slave or a few individuals is insufficient.
3
Understand the rationale
If the restriction took effect secretly, those who traded with the slave would be harmed because their debts would be postponed until after the slave's emancipation, and the slave's earnings are not attached to the debt.
This is a rational proof based on avoiding harm (darar).
4
Apply to various scenarios
Consider the text's examples: restriction in the market with few people vs. in the house with most market people present, and the analogy to an agent's dismissal.
The criterion is notoriety, which substitutes for direct notification to everyone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عبد مازون کو آقا نے مجبور کر دیا تو وہ کب مجور ہوگا
قال فان حجر عليه لم ينحجر حتى يظهر حجره بین اهل سوقه لانه لو انحجر لتضرر الناس به لتاخر حقهم الى ما بعد العتق لما لم يتعلق برقبته وكسبه وقد بايعوه على رجاء ذلك ويشترط علم اكثر اهل سوقه حتى لو حجر عليه فى السوق وليس فيه الارجل اورجلان لم ينحجر ولو بايعوه جازوان بايعه الذى علم بحجره ولو حجر عليه فى بيته بمحضر من اكثر اهل سوقه ينحجر والمعتبر شيوع الحجر واشتهاره فيقام ذلك مقام الظهور عند الكل كما في تبليغ الرسالة من الرسول ويبقى العبد ماذونا الى ان يعلم بالحجر كالوكيل اذ لم يعلم بالعزل وهذا لانه يتضرر به حيث يلزم قضاء الدين من خالص ماله بعد العتق وما رضى به وانما يشترط الشيوع فى الحجر اذا كان الاذن شائعا اما اذا لم يعلم به الا العبد ثم حجر عليه بعلم منه ينحجر لانه لا ضرر فيه
When the master has compelled (restricted) the ma'dhun slave, when does he become restricted? He said: For if he (the master) restricts him, he is not restricted until his restriction becomes apparent among the people of his market. Because if he were restricted, people would be harmed by it, as their right is postponed to after emancipation, since it does not attach to his raqabah and earnings, and they dealt with him in hope of that. And the knowledge of most of the people of his market is a condition. So if he restricts him in the market and there are only one or two men, he is not restricted. And if they dealt with him, it is permissible. If the one who knew of his restriction dealt with him, it is not permissible. And if he restricts him in his house in the presence of most of the people of his market, he is restricted. And the criterion is the notoriety and spread of the restriction, so that stands in place of appearance to everyone, as in the delivery of a message from the messenger. And the slave remains permitted until he knows of the restriction, like an agent who is not informed of dismissal. This is because he would be harmed by it, as he would be obliged to pay the debt from his pure property after emancipation, and he did not consent to that. And notoriety is required in the restriction when the permission was notorious. But if only the slave knew of it, then if the master restricts him with his knowledge, he is restricted because there is no harm in it.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage discusses when the master's restriction (hajr) on the ma'dhun slave becomes effective. According to the Hanafi school, the restriction does not take effect until it becomes public knowledge (shuyu' wa ishtihar) among the people of the market. This is because if it took effect secretly, people dealing with the slave would be harmed, as they had relied on his apparent permission and had given him credit. Therefore, the condition is that most market people know. If the master restricts the slave in the market but only a few people are present, it is not effective. However, if the restriction is done in his house in the presence of most market people, it is effective. The slave remains permitted (ma'dhun) until he learns of the restriction, like an agent who is not affected by dismissal until he knows. This is to prevent harm to the slave, as otherwise he would have to pay debts from his own pure property after freedom, which he did not consent to. But if only the slave knew of the permission, then restricting with his knowledge is effective because no harm to third parties.

Key Terms
حجر (hajr): restriction imposed by the master on the ma'dhun slave preventing him from trading
شيوع (shuyu'): notoriety or widespread knowledge of the restriction among the market people

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What makes the master's restriction (hajr) on the ma'dhun slave effective?
A) The master's verbal statement alone.
B) Knowledge of most market people.
C) The slave's acknowledgment.
D) The presence of witnesses.

Key Takeaway
The master's restriction on a ma'dhun slave is only effective when it becomes notorious among market people, protecting innocent dealings.
